When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the divisions of treatment, and it does not improve, then they resort to three methods of cauterization that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	When there is one method in which you make three or four cauteries, lining up according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cauterization that we have mentioned before; and do not press your hand too much on the whole cauterization, and let the hairs be near its back; and another method of cauterization is that you heat the cauterization that has two needles, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the wound which is near the mouse, or the ear of the hurt side, and let the elevations that you lift the wound according to its curve, according to the length of the body, and the cauterization should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After giving the first two nerves, burn until the needle is perceived from the other side, and then remove the cautery, and thus enter into four. If you see, then cauterize with the entire cautery at three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gotten purulence by long tension, and this is worth mentioning that the other cures mentioned above should be done.
de ydropisie	of hydrops
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not good for hydrops, except in the manner which is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods that we have mentioned in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the belly, and one above the stomach, and one above the liver, and one above the spleen, and one behind the back above the spine, and one at the worst place; and let the cauteries be very close to the surface of the skin.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After the fire cautery is applied for purification long and tight, and do not leave the care of the wound after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and together with God's help, the two intentions will be achieved.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the fire cautery for the belly is as shown before; and for the back, it is an olive branch, as it is shown before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen to one who is hydroptic, and are plain of yellow bile, it is necessary that you cauterize above the foot between the auricular and annular; and let your hand with the cautery towards returning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply into the flesh, thus avoiding damaging the nerves, and let the cauterizer follow this form:

de la menoison	of the menstruation

de plaie mal curee	of poorly treated wound

de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys

de la vessie	of the bladder

de la marris	of the marsh

de la hainche	of the hip

de la dolor dou dos	of great pain two

de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of the joints is due to moisture that has spread to each member of the body, and when the pain comes in a foot, which is properly called "podagra", and when it is caused by cold and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this manner: apply much cauterization around the joint of the foot, and let the cauterizing oil be applied in this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a mark on the face of the pet that you should prick, then cauterize the entire cauterization that is called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come from the knees and other joints, and it happens often, then cauterize with three or four cautery irons on each part of the cauterization olive; and if you have more skill, do more, but do not hold your hand further than the edge of the curved iron.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, then administer the cauterization that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	If the pains are in the fingers, then make pinpricks two lines wide; and if they remain unchanged, make pinpricks above each joint and above the hair of the hand; and if the pains come from the wrist or shoulder, cauterize each part, and give good advice to the patient and apply appropriate medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give good advice and purge the humor, it will be healed by the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the tearing of the gums
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When tearing comes in anger, and the bowels descend to the thighs and this is new, then it is necessary that when you see him to heal, that he not move much that day; and that he use things that lessen the belly, so that the flesh does not fall from his belly; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his jaw until the bruises are repaired, and the teeth in his hand, and sign with a seal of healing above the bone of the thumb, and at all signs that are similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and drips blood.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then remove the mud from the shoulder; and let the ministers stain their hands over it so they do not return; and work well on the thighs with the pain, and put disinfectant on him, the tincture and the sergeant on the thighs, and the other above the least that stains his hands; then put the cautery on the sign across your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again with another until you come just short of the bone; and be careful that the mud does not come out while you are doing the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this way the pain does not die, or any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And if you do not reach the bone with the fire cautery, your work is useless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the fire cautery for children should be applied subtly according to their measure, and for large people in proportion; after three days, care for the wound of the fire cautery until the scab is formed; then care for other inflammations until it is healed, and grind the hairs on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that their movements be restricted for a long time, so that the blisters do not form when they move around in rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, he should be given a well-made bandage, and wear it for another forty days; and he should have good rest, that he does not work too much and avoids too much drinking and eating, and too much high breathing; and if he follows this instruction, he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will tell you what to do after the cure of cutting into his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the tearing of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When tears come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, then apply the fire cautery according to its quantity, and let the third part of the wound be covered; after the cure according to what we have said; and no one of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized with the fire cautery at three angles in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but the first sign is the shoulder blade and make a line across the width of the rent, and another below, and hold your hand over all the burns with the cauterizing iron.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cautery is lighter and less painful.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, or to fall or to wound, and this pain lasts long, and the cure of medicine does not help, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cauteries should follow the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its power and its location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is safe to perform the first cauterization, it is good; if not, begin another cauterization above that one, for it is usually customary that it must die to the member that is closest, because it is necessary that you perform the cauterizations until the hairs are healed.
de meselerie	from masturbation
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Masturbation is never helped by cauterization, and at the same time the disease that comes from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you see that the cauterization does not help, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and if it does not spread or stay, and you doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the injury, then make three cauterizations: I on the forehead, and the other towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and II above the two corners, and I behind the temple; and leave as much hand as the cauterization comes just to the bone, and as much as the scabs come out so that the vapors of the large humors can escape; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the fracture is scattered throughout; and it is clearly manifest, so you must cauterize with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and the cautery in the back of the neck, and two cauteries above the spine of the neck, and six cauteries above the spine of the back, and one great above the buttocks and one other below, and two above the shoulders, and two above the elbows, and two above the knees, and one above each joint of the hands and feet, and above the wounds of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are above the backbone, that you do not burn them; and never make a cautery above the bone of the little finger, and one above the bone of the stomach, and one above the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And the more you do cauterization, the less you help, and it harms him; and know that the hairs do not feel pain as the healthy ones do, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	It should be that the cauterization is large and small according to the members and the joints, as you will find in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After curing the wound with flour and honey and other cures until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes in any member and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then you should cauterize above the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization be a little inside the skin of the cure; then the cure of ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never cauterize with the hand and the foot and the back, at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus it is ossified the swelling; and all the while do not intervene if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	Et aucune fois fait on caut
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is awakened, and medical knowledge does not help, then cauterize it with a cautery a little in front, according to the quantity of the curative bark, until the swelling is ossified and its color changes; then treat it with flour of wheat and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and sand from colon and sand from almond, each part separately; and mix everything together, and bind it on the affected area, and apply it to the affected area until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of chancre by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When chancre appears at the beginning, and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cauterizer that seems to be in the shape of a circle, all around the edge of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all the wise say that one should also make a cauterizer in the middle of the chancre; and I do not think it is good, because I believe it will not become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never seen it happen once; and a better thing is that it be cauterized all around, with the cauterizer that is called «circle», as we have said in many cauterizers.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the inflammation which cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called "adubelati", and it is slow to die out, either due to the excess it causes or due to the sharpness of the pain when they are very old (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to the tension; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauteries, holding it; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing the whole cauterization, then heat the cauterization from where this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" until the cauteries pierce the skin, and let them be such cauteries that the hairs feel afterwards in a similar way as the course of the pustule is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until they are completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another way of disease is called "corrodens", and is nothing other than a kind of member, for it bends the members as if the dry branches were bent.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the leg that can suffer cauterization together with fire, then heat the cauteries deeply and greatly, according to what is needed for the leg or the disease; after cauterizing all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put oil on the wounds, cauterize with suffering until the scorches of fire are removed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of inflammations, they generate ulcers.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy ulcers do not arise, it is good; and if not, if you begin the cauterization again on what remains of the wounds corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this method has never been cured by medicine in place of the fire cauterization; but the fire cauterization is always greater help, and I have already told the cure of the medicine ailment in the division: take it when you have business.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the pearls that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times, when they come to the feet by mistake, a disease is born that is called "closed" according to our understanding, and it is a great thing that causes pain in the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries of this disease are according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to say, fire cauterization, and ice-hot cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cauterization is that you heat the cauterizer as if it were a pen of ink, and it is made of good iron at the measure that it can pierce the nail from all parts, and that it has thin margins; then put it all hot on top of the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it reaches the end of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to rot; then make an ointment of wild, ground spices with silk, and leave the ointment all night, and the nail will close and will be removed from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the limb with a poultice until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by the horse's feet, and often in hands and feet, then it is necessary to apply cauterization with very hot iron; and it is done in this way: take an iron or iron needle, or a quill pen, and place it on the nail and the wart, that is, put the warts on; then put a little hot water in it, hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the iron comes to the root of the nail, and find the very hot water going deep into the root; and let the pain of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will all fall out at its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Next do another one, until you have exhausted all those that are in the chest, then cure the wounds that engender char.
li cure dou trembler	The cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone trembles from cold or from the fourth-day fever or other, it is necessary to make four cautery burns or four on the spine of the back; one cautery between each spine; and one cautery on the belly, and one on the stomach at the cautery olive; it will leave the trembling, and hasten the recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	Of pus-filled boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No case has ever been seen where the body, bathed in sweat, or covered in pustules, was infected by large corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary when they appear that one perform a fire cauterization above each pustule: a subtle cauterizing iron from mugwort, of which the point is grasped in the fire, or from the root of aristolochia, or with the lenticular cauterizer.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never cauterize them at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, and it cannot grow more, but is broken up the excess from which they come, and are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	often there is great loss of blood from the cut artery at the wound that comes from the surrounding area, or at the incision of the abscess, or in cauterizing the member, and similar things; and it is a very painful thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, you must quickly place your finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it tightly until the blood is no longer flowing out; then apply the heated cauterizing irons in various sizes both small and large until they are all red; then apply a larger or smaller one according to the size of the wound and the part where the artery is located, and hold the cautery on that vein where you place your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if you lift your other hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another one that is at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the bleeding stops; and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that other harm does not come to the wound; and see that when the artery is not cut, it cannot be extinguished directly when the artery is large, unless by one of the four ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not yet treated, or by a very fine thread, or by medicines placed on which have power to stop bleeding.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers tightly binding bandages or hot objects above, or similar things, does not benefit unless they do not.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no other remedy or medicine present, they should place their finger index above the wound of the vein as we have said, and tightly bandage it until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and they should not move it, but often dab it with very cold water until it is frozen and swollen and stopped; and make inquiries about what remedies and medicines are available.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of remedies for wounds
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases for which it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or with burning medicine, and the symptoms and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I will put this chapter about the shoulder joint just below, and I will go to this chapter by that same way in order to find out more easily what we want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore when I begin this chapter, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and therefore it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you should not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such people who are so with their illness that they die immediately because of the harm they receive from their disease, and the greatness of its evil; and of these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these, there are those who give you their meaning, and say: "wait, I am sharp"; and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It does not matter only that you allow those who come to you who have this way, but put greater caution in your honor than in your desire, and do not open rashly but wisely of what you are certain, and which you have taken and lost; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your diseases for salvation to be converted; and this will help you to achieve good reputation, glory, and memory for a long time.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lords give you good understanding and straightness, and if you wish to breathe from the holy inspiration of his hand, indeed.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have already ordered you this chapter by dividing it into parts, according to what is before a chapter on cauteries, which I have divided from the top down, so that you will find it easier to understand what you will have to do.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full of sharp
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often occurs in children when they are born, and when the midwife's hand is too tightly held, the child's head; and sometimes it comes from a reason that one is not aware of.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and all those that I have seen died; and because it seems to me that it is better to learn the work in these treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	I saw a child who was complaining of severe pain in the shoulder, and the head was swelling each day until it could no longer bear it; and he thought so much of the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled outside the bone above the joint, between the skin and the bone; and the treatments are such that if the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a wide cut on the head; and it should be as long as II, so that the moisture flows out; and then remove the shape of the spatumile.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more extensive, and the abscess is larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form.
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the commissures of the neck opened on each part, and the sharp pain when you press it with your hand from inside, and it has not returned to you: then it is necessary that you make three cuts in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture out.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After extracting the cuts with gauze and powders, and putting wine and oil on it, leave it in place for five days; then remove it, and treat the wound with bandages and counter-irritation, and keep the head still, and give small amounts of dry food with a little moisture until the limb is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look for the largest opening of the abscess, and the gathering of the sharp edge; for it is never in front, never behind, never to the right, and never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore cut where the abscess is open, and fill it with the sharp edge, and make the incision according to what you can; and be careful not to cover the artery; and if blood flows, then the patient may die from the flow of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	I'm sorry, I don't understand
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it has to do with one disease called "cataract" in the eyes or at the bottom, and the disease is ancient, and the medical cure does not help much, then the other cure is to cauterize with what is used to cover the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, while you look at them, it is necessary that the hairs of their head be made to stand on end; then rub the affected area with a rough cloth until the arteries are visible, then hold the hairs against the entire cloth; then look where the vein lies, and the roots of both are behind the ears, and they are not returned; then sign the roots of the ears, then cover both with a two-pronged forceps until the wound comes just to the bone, and it should be through the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, push the two-pronged forceps away from the artery and cover it above, cutting as if it should go through the middle.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if blood flows out continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open when felt, then measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then sign it and pierce into the bone; and what is necessary to put in the abscess is six centimeters, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the wound can suffer, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone point not deep, then cut the skin that we have sutured, and then close and bind the wound, and treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of the head
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient headache comes, and the catarrh is severe, due to the moisture of tears and the chills in the temples and the old age and similar things, and it is treated with methods of medical cures and nothing seems to help, then we should cauterize the arteries of the temples, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is such that the hairs of his temples face backwards, and one listens to the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and it is only slightly replaced in anyone who is too cold; and if it is replaced, then one strains the skin with some cloths, then rubs the skin with some rough cloth, and bathes the skin in hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula of which this form is made:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then cut it upwards with pincers, and remove all the webs that are adhered to each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it back to the tip of the scalpel, then cover that part according to the amount of the two incisions.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not covered, it will not heal completely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out a lot of blood from the sixth vein, just to the third; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong silk thread, which does not allow any blood to come before the healing of the wound, and does not allow any clots to form; then cover the excess that is between the two threads in the same hour, and then, if you see, if the fire cautery is applied just to the bone until the incisions are covered; and this is the most difficult work, if the pains are not feverish and he is of hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	Because the cautery is to finally finish the moisture: because it is of greater help to moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with old cotton and place dry bandages; and when they are removed, take care of dry medicines that produce heat and bandages until they are healed; and if without cutting the artery as you have worked, then hasten to cover it with a cauterizer, or fill the wound with vinegar and apply it to your hand that the wound is not frozen; and if you do not have this present, then place ice on the wound for as long as the wound is not frozen, and raise the limb in cold water until it is completely healed, and it is stretched as it should be; and what is more difficult and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cauterizer cutting from II parts, but the cuts should be well spaced to last longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the instrument is too tight, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a great space, and then when you have marked the two lines, and you melt the hot iron above so that it comes just to the bone, and cover the vein in two lines; and they should be separated between the two cuts because it is not known of this cauterization at all; and this is the form of the cauterization:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are dripping from veins that are above the skin of the forehead, and it does not benefit at all from medical treatment, and you see the face of the patient becoming twisted, and it feels as if it is shaking; and the hair is held and moist so that the hairs of the forehead are wet, and the papers are torn, and they are burned by the heat of the tears, if there is a need for this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they would call the ancient "cure of contusions", and you should do the following to the hair that has this disease, whether it is on the front or not; then make three cuts evenly along the length of the front; and one of the cuts as if two are completely through the front by going down from the nose, and the others two at the ribs above the papers, and be careful of the incision of the arteries that are at the ribs above the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound have the quantity of three drops across the joins; and have a piece of sponge and much cloth ready to soak up the blood, then pour the herb in two parts where this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made from the temple up to the second incision; and scrape off everything that is between the two cuts from the top of the bone, then make another cut on the other side of the same incision, and then extract this bone fragment.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you insert the tool called "curette" into the first cut, which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, and it is shaped like this:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side of the curette towards the cartilage and the blunt side towards the bone, and continue to scrape until it reaches the same cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for all the vessels that descend from the chief as far as the eyes, continue the incision until the court is open, and then make another incision in the same place on the other side; then extract the blood equally, and press the wound for the blood taken; then put a piece of old cotton in each incision, and put moistened cloths with wine and oil and vinegar on top, and guard against abscesses not coming; and the next day remove the bandage, and apply a great amount of salted herbs, then the cure of ointment basilicon with rose oil, and other cures that are used to heal wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	return of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any come to cautery with custom, and you see the eyes closed and small, and weakened vision, and burnt papers; and the hairs are shaved, and where the shaving is done, it causes pain, and the hairs are sneezed out; therefore, by these accidents that those matters and cautery do not come from only many veins, and the movement that is there, if this is so.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And whether you command the patient to turn his head back, then make a great cut across the forehead, and another wide down to the eye.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the cut on the right temple to the left temple, and let the incision be just to the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at the pain; and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood onto a sponge, and then clean between the two lips of the cut and put in old cotton, and cover with linen; then bind above with moistened cloths soaked in wine and oil, and guard against abscess forming; when it is removed, it is necessary to rub the bone until charcoal begins to appear, then treat with things that cause sweating, which are used to remove char.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of collyrium, and make a poultice; and apply it to the wounds to draw out the charcoal throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the ear deafness
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that sticks in the ear is one of the four things: either grains or wax or stone or similar thing like iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas; or things that run down, such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it sticks in the ear or any other kind of thing that does not fit well in the ear, it does not grow in the ear, so put the ear to the sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the arrow, if any drops of purple oil or hemlock oil are distilled, then apply extraction; and this is to make him vomit of condition, and stop his nose when he sneezes, and put around his ear pieces of cloth or wool; and raise his ear.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often comes out by this cure; and if it does not come out, then apply extraction with thin needles, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by the needles, it is good; if not, apply extraction with a thin, double-edged needle; and if it does not come out by this, then take a rain-stick and fill the hole of the rain-stick or the ear canal very full of wax so that nothing can enter with the stick; then pull it out carefully, for often comes out like we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, then take glue of which they take the eyes, and put it on some instrument that is sharp for this purpose, and put a little cotton around; then press the glue above the arrow or whatever, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not jump from all these things that we have said, then quickly break the ear to stop the abscess and blood flow, and spasms; and the way of breaking is that you first make a small incision in the place of the pain, and extract the pus according to its strength, then place the pus between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat or flesh depends; and let the incision be as smooth as a moon, until you reach the bone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck vigorously at your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is small and swollen, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer the following subtle form of suction:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision in that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make a large incision when you think the grains are moist due to earwax, until you have made many pieces; then extract them with small forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of an earache, it is necessary to use steam from a conditioned first, and widen the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it lie across the very ear itself where the sharp point is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out due to the wind, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If the wind does not, take many thin and light stones according to the length of your thumb, and warm them in the fire; and place the hairs of one ear, and move upwards from the other foot, and strike with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease to do this stone after stone until the sharp point is all out, and thus it jumps out all out; and if you see, take the reed, and blow one of the hairs into the ear, and the other hair take with fire until the thinnest reed is burnt; then make the other side similar to what we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is small in size, such as a mouse and similar things, proceed as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then use pincers for extraction; and it is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, if you treat them as we have said in the division and if the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to look into the ear with the sun: if there are no worms, then use fine pincers to remove them; if there are none, then take the candle of this form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And use a more subtle chisel in the ear according to the amount of pain, then it is often successful throughout the bone; do this as often as all of them are seen.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to extract, then bend the bone around with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they cannot be extracted as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have experimented with in the extraction of arrows, and you will find them where treating distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it is of silver or lead, make small holes in the bottom and larger ones on top to pour through; and to press during distillation, use a well-made instrument of lead for this purpose, and if you see a razor and wrap cotton around its point evenly; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you see in the container, and the container should be in the ear; then squeeze through the razor all the cotton, and press your hand constantly until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear; and feel the bad smell inside, and the distillation should be just slightly warmed over the fire, as it is distilled into the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear congestion
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some congestion in their ears; and this also happens to men by ear congestion, or by a hardening of the inside of the ear, and this congestion never comes from within the ear, if one cannot see it; and it never comes from a lack of congestion, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That congestion which comes from within the ear, if one cannot see it, is due to great sickness in many positions, and in this one where one sees that you must put the ear with the bad pain in the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening, then the work of this length of time is the form of what is inside.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be ausculted and percussed all around, so that it does not cause the ear to bleed; if the opacification is of charcoal or of the ear bone, then hold the ear with fine forceps, and the copper lightly, until that charcoal is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opacification is in front of the ear, then take a fine razor lightly and heat it slightly over the fire, then put it on the bone of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the opacification that causes the patient to have a gritty sensation in the ear, percuss lightly, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the size of the pustule, and moisten it with Egyptian medicine.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not perform any action until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rosewater, and powder it with vitriol; if you see pus flowing from the ear, then it is necessary to remove the tent and apply another tent made of rosewater and wax, until the discharge stops; then cure it as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if blood flows out, soak a sponge and wipe it with cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the flow of blood, which are either to treat the distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method for removing thorns from papers when they are wet and dry: you should stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and remove the root with a piece of glass; then apply vitriol to the wound.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they cannot be removed without cutting, then cauterize the wound with a fine lens caustic, and the cauterizer after incision is suitable; many times they repair, but nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the sand
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Frequently, in papers, there are things that seem to be gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this disease is called "hail", and it is an assembly of large moisture above and below the paper; the work is such: if the hail moves from one side to another, and it is a light thing to know; then make the wound wide, then scrape each part lightly, then take it with pincers, and the cloth.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not cover it with a cloth without piercing the paper, it does not harm the wound; and if the wound is large, it should be sown up as soon as possible; and if it is small, do not force it, for the inflammation will return quickly and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the splinter is large and falls into the depths of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the splinter in a pair of pliers, and hold and press it on both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it causes no harm; and when the splinter is removed, apply a drop of strong salt water to the wound, and cure the ear of any injury until the wounds are healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is smeared on paper above the eyes, and it has more in children than in adults, and it causes much pain to their eyes, and they vomit it in the morning, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears flow to their eyes; and because they lie on their faces, they sleep on them, and their papers are outside their eyelids moist, which swells and covers their appearance with the exinach that appears in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint to your touch and feel the grinding between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the work is such that the bones put their head in your hand; then take a piece of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount that contains the grinding from each part, then place it on top of it; and press from one side and the other, so that the grinding is assembled inside the circle; then cutting into the moisture at the edge of the blade a slit of a large width, and not any larger than the wound on the skin of the vein; and cut the skin until you come to the grinding; and in many positions of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the entire piece of cloth from between your two hands, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to insert into the wound, that you do not bring the whole cloth up to the oil, that you do not wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not extend at the beginning of the wound, then slightly tear the wound until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then smooth the cloths in hot and cold water, and put on the limb, and spread it well with ointment.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who breathe and put on them to corrupt the moisture that is remaining.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as they are healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient comes with an abscess that is not yet ready, then the healer should apply wet compresses until they are healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
