Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers are born with hairs that are not natural, and they are awake, if they harm the eyes, and bring on various diseases such as tears and softening of the papers and cornea, until it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cauterization with fire together, or by medicine blister according to what is before or chapter of cauterization, and is done or by incision and stitching or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the pain in your hand, then turn the paper of oil to your right hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is an arrow at all the thread above; and let the thread under the margin of the paper where the hair grow among these hairs, and pull the thread above the whole paper, and return to the razor; then in the part outside the paper, outside the hairs adjusted, all the skin painting, from the great calf just to the small; then stretch the thread, and place outside the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then above the paper a figure of an anchor, like the full moon, and in all cases it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you saw lift the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it is a patient who has experience with great quantities of paper according to how the paper is softened; then make all the space above the two lines that you have marked, and start from the large calf downwards; and soak one of the wounds near the natural hairs in the root of a large one, then squeeze the ink into one of the two angles of the quill, then scrape off the skin; then gather the two lips to one seam of an needle with all the thin silk thread, and wipe the blood, and dry the excess hairs above the two sides in any way that you see fit; and if not, if you do not have care for it, then leave the seam and the threads for three days or four; then cure the wound from the sides of things that are dry and constricting, because the paper reattaches to the suddenness of the wound and the assembly of it, but the seam is dried (as they say of the ancients), and this is work without fear; and if in another way: and it is that you sign the paper in a figure that is as like the shape of the mirror as we have told, at three places according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply force evenly according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or have a thread, and bend it into the shape; and bend the other thread over the big arm, and the second thread over the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin where you have sewn, as we have told you, then assemble the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with carron oil and similar soothing ointments; and never once have the hairs of the skin turned: if you use what we have said about the incision, but sewing in one and out the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The care of wounds is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and the bandage inside according to what I have said, and then make two wounds by art, and two subtle threads as long as the paper and the width of the space is; and cope with the two ends where you hold the threads; then gather the one and the other subtly above what is above the paper of the oil, and strain the two wounds from the two parts form; and leave it in this way for some time, and the skin that was stretched will die and rot and produce, as long as it falls by it.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it lingers, if the copper has some force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound has been suppurated, and if the paper has been lifted, and they will not grow back; and this is the form of the two kinds of plasters that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The methods are such that you grasp a fine needle, and pull the silk thread softly and finely; then assemble the heads and no the one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order the other thin silk thread briefly, and do not tie the heads of the thread; then put the hairs on your skin, and so it is declined, for this is a thin and small bandage, then pull the needle through the whole bandage at the base of the hair raised, and pierce it into the paper gently until you draw it over the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the bandage, and pull in the bandage that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out all over the bandage with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the patient is chased and treated, and the hairs do not grow back with it, then treat the chase with the discharge as you have ordered, until the chase comes out completely and you can see it through the oil; then treat the chase and the thread, and close the oil and let it rest for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and grows on the skin; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the goats naturally, and raise it with the one you leave, until it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purity of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the "porridge", comes into the oil, there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it comes by means of wounding, or cutting, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment in this case is to break that suture, and dry the lips of it, and put in tents of linen, and bind it until it is healed; and you should only use in its care things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will become worse than before; but in the work of things that are softening, such as fenugreek; and the rose of sharp or high and seeds of linen are cooked, and pungent ingredients of quicksilver melted in any of the oils, and there is wrapped a tent, and the care of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you take care not to let them be spoiled according to their former form; and this work that we have said is no other than a guide against this disease, that it does not return according to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the chariot that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and cut and cauterization and similar things; and the method of the work is that you hold an needle, in which it has double thread, and the skein in the chariot, and make it pierce from the left arm to the right, so that the thread comes out in two threads of the chariot; then place the char above all the needle, and the covering wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper returns to its original shape according to what it should be, it is good; if not, take the razor and put it in the groove, and turn the paper, and make two cuts or corners inside the paper; and let the two wounds from the two angles of the incision you have made meet, and make a corner so that when they are assembled, the shape is as if it were a letter with no «Greek»; then remove that char, according to the quantity that its cost is not from, from what the paper teaches, then add the two missing parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then cure as we have said about the medicines that soften, and tents, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a wound or stitching or cauterization, it is necessary to make a plain slit between the hairs of the skin, and according to what has been said before; then cleanse between the two sheets of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters apply various methods of all sorts to make the figure return to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for the work and tools in many different positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	The skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this stitching is done by unskilled people in a certain way, where the paper above is smeared with the white of oil, and cannot move or do their work naturally, then you should go outside the paper with the point of a razor, and lift it up; and extend it with pincers, until you scrape off what is hard to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or too rough, so that the hairs cannot suffer that the spatula is too sharp or burns the oil; and your incision, from which you scrape off that assembly, should be lightly made, so that the paper regains its natural form; and that whole assembly is healed, and nothing is ever done in vinegar and salt oil, and lifted with vinegar and decoction; then place between the paper and the oil a linen cloth, and put on top of the oil moistened wool; and after the job use decoction and other healing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the elbow of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two ways in which the elbow is affected: one is nervous and resembles a hard, rough, facial skin, and another that is not nervous but resembles white frozen moisture, so that when touched with iron and heated with pliers, it cannot be removed; and both start from the large arm, grow slowly and slowly until they cover the entire eyelid and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is such that the hairs put their head in your hand, then work the eyes; and lift the paper to your hand, then bend the elbow with pliers of small doubled, and extend it above; then take a needle, and put the hair of a horse, or a cow, or a beef, and the thread strongly; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the elbow, and push the needle through the whole needle, and tie the elbow with a thread and extend it above, and scrape all the hair on the side of the elbow that extends to the prickle and the silk at the hair just below, then cover the remaining in the root of the arm to the most subtle spatula and with small forces, and leave the natural skin of the arm, so that by the incision does not come the usual tears; and once it was extended only to the elbow, and at the thread, as we have said; then scrape all the soft spatula of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the charred flesh and break it, and that the prunel is not pierced; and after the incision pour a little bit of broken silk oil, and a collar made of litargire, and leave it just above the other wound; then care for the wound until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the joint is not numb, and you cannot insert the needle, and the pins cannot enter, many times this resembles a joint of medicines; and they are born as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the oil of the pain, and take the spatula lightly with a sharp edge according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently rub the joint above, and if you see that it does not ease and the pain persists, then pour from your mouth into the oil colier made of litargire and red oil and silk broth, and extinguish the oil just after; then start the other work according to this same method, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, as with an abscess, then milk it, and cure the abscess thoroughly until it is healed, then start the work again as before, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh on the arm shows signs of great harm in oil by night, then soak it in vinegar and apply a part and not all at once, until tears do not come; then pour in oil a red wine colloid which is made from litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the hair that grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men's hairs never grow red, and cover the pupil and restrain above the papers and turn back to the defense, and it seems like a baluster rose; and if the work is that the hairs put their head in your skin, then work the eyes, and cut all those hairs with suitable nicks to this, and support it at force; then cover the first hair, and go all scraping to the razor just to the end, and be careful not to wound the oil at the work; and let the incision of the spanish that we have said in the incision of the nail and as small forces of which we take the base, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is accomplished and all the hairs are removed, then use the oil of silk beaten or you distill red wine colloid and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil behind cotton with abin of wool, so that it is ensured not to have an abscess; and if nothing remains, and the skin does not cover, and you doubt an abscess, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with calming abscess medicines; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make all the hairs that are adjusted in the oil by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you apply the care of each weakness of the natural pathway; and of the accidental pathway, in iron work; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member suffers from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes'
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins that are covered over the eye, and take away from the view their work and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, the first thing you should look at in the eye is whether it is clear or not, and there is no other disease besides that; then prescribe the following remedy: command the patient to put his head in your safe place, then soak those veins all around according to their wisdom, and let the soaking be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two in degrees in one course according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then apply those forces gently, and suck out the pus an hour after another, until you can remove those veins from the oil; and be careful not to prick the oil with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cope with those veins; and when you have done this, pour green and red wine distillate into the oil to corrupt what remains from before.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all the blood in that hour, then apply a plaster on the oil of things that ease the pain of the eyes, and let it stay for some time until the pain is eased and you are sure there is no abscess, then begin again according to this method as long as it is healthy; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	If the mirror is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with fire and medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, then make an incision above the abscess, where it must die, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is revealed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is revealed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then remove all the instrument that this is made of; and it is called "hard head", and make a new one from fair iron as from the previous one, and point it as a lime if it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place above the broken bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a little until you feel that corruption is removed; do this once, then restore the broken bone with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is sound, and the flesh has grown, and the body of the wound is sound, and remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen and is not abscessed, and no bad accidents come, then remove it when it is healed; if not, there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula to the perforation of the bone according to this form: and you should uncover the bone the second time by fire, and by wet medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the iron according to this form, and make it thin at the top as you see fit.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it above the bone of the arm, and move your hand away from the oil and the pain, then return to the full extent of the forearm until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the pain if they hold their hand above their neck; and when the medicine is dry, as I have indicated, and when the char heals and hardens the limbs, then apply the matter to the neck; it is a lighter thing for the pain.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open widely and do not stir, nor are they disturbed or soothed, then you must bind the pain; then clean it, then apply leeches or a blister to draw out the poison, then put on the oil mixed with acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocollis, and then strain the oil, and apply it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths that are soft enough, and double each in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes have had; then strain it through a thick, strong cloth, and restart the leeches or blister to draw out the poison without causing pain; then remove the leeches and leave the oil strained day and night, and if the eyes are not restored, it is good; if they are, then remove the dressing and the oil and the leeches and the blister and start again with the bandages and cloths and the oil until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The breaking of a silk thread
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the silk thread, then open, and come forth with force as if a grain of resin, and it is easy to see; then if you see it covered, the work is such that you would drive a needle into the root of the part below this above, then drive another needle or where there is double the thickness of the arm; and pierce it, and let the first needle follow its position; then cover the doubled thread and tie a part of the silk around, and hold it well, then extract the needle and put on the other side of the oil in abundance of honey; and let it stay until the silk thread has healed with the wound, then care for the oil of things comforting until the wound is healed; and never once does the wound need to be covered by a piece of cloth from a circle, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear greatly distorted, pierce them with a fine needle that comes from the spine, and remove the moisture and drain it away from the eyes, and enter there at once; then extract them until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the spine
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing more than a bone that is assembled in the spine, appearing sharp and descending, but it is not actually sharp; and the manner of its appearance in the work is such that you make the patient sit with the misaligned part straight and high, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move the mouth until you see the bone coming up to your eyes; then sew it, and do not drain it and let it be dissolved by light, and see the things as they should be; and if it does not descend, it is sharp, and if it descends from the bone, it is not straight as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the painful part between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make it over the corneal thread and the crown, as long as the bow is released; and when it is released, then pour hot, sharp oil mixed with honey, or sharp or fenugreek boiled and honey, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the sharp oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have similar sharp oils in the division, and what is necessary to pierce; so work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary for you to make the dislocated joint sit between your crossed hands, outside of the light for the sun, and apply clean and tightly stretched oil; then place the oil paper in your right hand if the joint is on the left side, or in your left hand if the joint is on the right side; then take in your right hand if the joint is on the left side, or in your left hand if the joint is on the right side, the instrument called «almagda»; then place the point of the instrument above the crown by the thickness of a rat in the blenchor of the oil at the part of the elbow, then forcefully push the instrument called «almagda» until it pierces into the blenchor of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the front of the measure of the space that is from the golden thread to the end of the needle; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cloth, then place the instrument above it where the sharp is, then expressly remove one after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If it is sharp now, then he sees the hairs in front of him and the tool in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, and if it is sharp again, go up the second way, put the forceps with the tool, and when it is well fixed and does not rise, gently pull around your hand little by little; then put a little thread gem in place, and leave it inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by default the eye is cleaned or in any way wet with rose oil and plenty of honey, and tie with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those who are our own, put on top with plenty of honey.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the oil cannot enter due to its hardness, because there are some men who have too hard eyes, then you must use the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Therefore, pierce only the conjunctive solely, and do not move too much in front, but make the eye subtle, then push the hardness, as we have said; and at the completion of the work compare to the pain and drowsiness occurring, in which it sleeps on its back in the dark room; and be still of all movements, and take light meals, and do not move its head to the right or left, and let it be tied according to its disposition just before this time; then release it in this same dark room, and prove its vision, and make it see some things, and then return the bandage after six hours; and you should not do this in the early morning of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you raise it, for that the sharp pain quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses appear, you should open them before the seventh hour, and relieve the swelling with what suppresses the abscess; and when it is calmed, remove the bandage and put on a new one to cover any opening, and let it stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then gradually leave the house little by little, and turn into your own case; and do not let any disciple intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Some came to us who were from the Yrach, who told us that in their country everyone gets sick with the disease, because of which the arrowhead is successful, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I read it in any books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of almadha, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are made of pure tin properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the heads are made from the same subtlety, and the rear in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the horn for the nose.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never are there any noses born or made that do not resemble each other, because there are some that seem like scorpions in the mouth of the feet; and if there are such ones, and if they have a horn enlarged of bad color, and if they have a nose of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that one of those noses which is soft, and not enlarged, it is necessary that you make the pain between your hands against the sun; and work its nostrils, and pour the essence of those noses, and the tailors away; because it corresponds to what you have sustained in the subtle spasm of a part, until you know that that nose is completely hard.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is nothing that can be covered, then open it with all the subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if it is a pustule, then cut it out as it should be; and if it is malignant pustules, then hasten and cauterize it until the wound is clean and all the poisons are removed, then pour out or drain the pus and apply a clean and sharp solution of wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the wound does not open properly, and moisture enters into the palate, then it is safe; and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, then there is a bone above, which prevents the instruments from cutting: therefore, you must use a piece of linen thread, and hold it with both hands, and space each needle between them as much or little as necessary; and put the hairs of the patient's head through the needle in their nostril at some distance, and pull out as much as possible through the nostril inside the mouth; and often they do this to children in schools, and it is a simple thing for someone who wants to do it; then hold the thread that comes out of the nostril with one hand, and the other thread that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and cut them alternately as if they were the threads we use.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you see that they have not corrupted that cloth, then remove the filth, soak the blood, and moisten the rag with Egyptian oil, and return it to the nose as before; do this three times or more, until the ointment has corroded all that remains of the cloth; then put or leave a plaster on the nose for several days until it is healed, and if there is need of dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, by which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, shaped like an open lamp, such as a cannon, and the conductor is used in the same way; and if you see, then make a closed cannon, and let the instrument for purging the head be plain, and have one hand on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the fire cautery
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	This disease often arises at the root of the nose and is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large over time; therefore, it is necessary to cover it at the beginning, and then apply the caustic or burning medicine; if it is difficult to cover it, check if it is hard, pale, and insensitive: if it is not touched by iron, it is a hidden abscess, for when it is covered, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is softly touched, not pale, and you see that it can be completely covered, then remove the disease and cure the patient of similar and restricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the bone is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	When solutions of continuity come in one of these cartilages, it is of little use, because in some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, if the wound is fresh and full of blood, and then close the two lips to a seam, then treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already decayed on one side and the other, then you must scorch all the parts that are not yet healed, then gather the two lips to a seam, and hold them together, and powder with powder of dragon’s blood, and burnt incense; and put the powders on a piece of strong or other plaster, and let it soak through, then treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of the stitching is such that you gather the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have abscesses within the lips, hard and small or larger ones; therefore it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut under each one, and take out the pus with pincers and clean every part; then apply the ointment after the incision of broken glass, until the wound is not soaked; then apply the oil, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the teeth's gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, abscesses arise above the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is necessary to hold them with forceps at their base and cut away the pus or blood; then apply a piece of broken glass powder, or other restrictive and desiccating powders; if the gum returns after incision and often does, then cut again and cauterize: if it still does not return after cauterization, these are the forms of instruments for covering.
des sordens	of the teeth
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the top of the teeth, between the gums, sharp and ugly scrape marks; and sometimes they are black and yellow and green, until corruption comes to the gum, and are black and smelly; it is necessary that you separate the bad between your hands, and its parts should be in your holy place, and cut the teeth or the scrape marks as long as there is nothing left; and thus make black and green, and yellow and jaundice and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if what is at the first level is good, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that the teeth have different forms of instruments for cleaning, according to what the work demonstrates, because the scraper used to clean between the teeth has other forms than those used to clean the teeth. And these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When treating a toothache, you should draw out as much of the pain as you can, for no one should do this; for it is a substance very high, just like that which we do not have an excuse to remove.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the tooth is painful from being drawn out, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth hurting.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the tooth is relieved, and one should check if it is a holy tooth, and draw out the bad tooth; and the pain does not depart immediately, because we have already done this to such saints; and when you are certain of the tooth hurting, it is necessary that you scorch around the tooth in all directions; then press it with your fingers or subtle forceps at the first and second joint, until it is well dislocated, then firmly hold the forceps; and let the one who is suffering from the pain in your holy mouth between your teeth, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After straightening the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump out, take any of these tools and push it lightly into each part, and shake it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and broken, it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the pulp is; and if the extraction is subtly hooked, so that it does not break when extracting; and it is very important to cover around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and if a part remains, it causes greater pain from the root of the first tooth.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act as the ignorant ones do, who, through haste and recklessness, break the cart once and for all, and never amend what we have told; but bring about great disease by the roots that they delay, or by the cart that they break, as often as we have seen; and when the dense matter is drawn out, wash the leg with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood comes, which often happens, use the leg of glass; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, by which one draws out the dense matter first, should be long and thick-billed, so that they do not double back when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And if they are large members such that they do not bend easily, and if they are made of iron well-made, and if they are teeth to hold the muzzle.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulling, then you must put soft cotton wool on the bone or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the bone is softened, then pull out the hooks called "algefri", of which the patient seems to have a beak; and they are made inside as a lime and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these hooks, then you must uncover the chisel completely around the root, and put the instrument called "althali", that is, the palainche, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be both thick and large so that it does not break easily, and if its root jumps out of the sky, it is good; if the sky does not, then with all the instruments, from which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it helps, use this instrument that has two prongs, from which this form comes:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument that seems like great tweezers, from which this form comes:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And it should be other tools that cannot break easily, and sharp enough that many dental tools are; and also other tools, which are not counted; and the wise masters find their own tool, according to their work and the disease shows them, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach the tool for the diversity of the use and if it does not break the cartilage or the other bones, or if it hurts, if it searches for tools that it should, as I have said, and helps with gestures, from which this form comes:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let the bones be large and well-held to keep them from escaping, but let him hold and remove; then restore the limb with appropriate medicines for this, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, then he should use all of this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course of the body, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, then it is necessary that you remove the tooth after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and no one can be made or polished: therefore, the rake; and if it is also with the tooth, take this instrument which is like a small beak, and is made of iron and sharp on top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the crown piece by piece in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that you can remove it, then the crown is removed with a piece of cloth like this is the shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the root of which we make arrows; and in the tooth, piece by piece in your hands lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks; then the plain at the end with any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, then you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when they are lost
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When they are lost, either by percussion or by falling out, and the teeth cannot be pressed upwards because of their position, and you treat them with restricting medicines, it does not help; then you should restrain them with a gold thread, for silver thread becomes green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth approaching each other, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the affected teeth between the healthy ones, as many as there are or more, until you feel secure on the other side; then begin again to cover the part where you started, and gently and skillfully press your hand, so that it does not move at all; and let your thread be tied to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the loose threads with a thread, and gather them together, and place them between the healthy teeth, so that they do not bleed the tongue; then leave them tightly closed for as long as possible, and if they loosen, or the threads break, then tie them again with another thread; if they still remain loose, and serve as such throughout their length, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two upper ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth chips, if it is reset in its place, from the front to the back, as we have said; and there is no interference that is not wise and painful, and never once has the shape of a sheep's tooth been made, and it is placed in the place where the defect is, and it is tied on as we have said, and it remains and serves as such throughout its length.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the tongue of the language
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There are no joints in the language that come out of the tongue or nature, which is born thus; or by accident of a wound, and the operations are such that you open the mouth with the painful tongue, and hold its head in your own, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous branch of the large, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it is hard or not, and it is from a severe wound, if you beat the honey and cut the large gently; and be careful that the wound is not too deep, for the artery that is out; and when you have done, lift the shoulder of high rose and oil, or high cold, then put out of the tongue a linen tent; and the painful tongues every night, so that the wounds do not stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, apply vitriol broken glass to the wound; and if it does not stop, cauterize with slow-burning fire, which is good for the skin; then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that the wound is of a yellowish or black color and hard, and it does not cause pain, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is inclined to suppuration and there is moisture, pour water through a thin sponge, and deliver from one side and the other; and if it does not stop bleeding at your work, apply broken glass until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you remove all the blood; then lift the wound off the sore and the skin, and treat with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	There is no time when boils that are called "godath" come from the throat, and they are properly called the second pustules, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then be careful: if they are hard to touch with a small sense and a brown color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the escape of blood; but let it be as long as it is alive, and then you will break it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is thin, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first check whether the abscess has settled and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit with the pain facing the sun, and his head tilted to one side, and the instrument in his hand, pressing the tongue out of the way, and the shape of it; and it should be made of silver or thin brass like some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the hook and the spoon into the wound, and scrape it out as much as you can; and take nothing else with it, then cover the instrument, which resembles a forceps, and the teeth are bent, one on top of the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have copper tongs, of which the form is like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And on one side, it is sharp, and on the other side, it is blunt; and when you have taken hold of one of the tongs, take hold of the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the sharp pain with hot, sharp, and cool water, and if there is blood flowing, gargle the sharp pain with hot water, or use pounded crab apples, or mint leaves, and similar things, until the wound is clean; then cure it until it is healed; and never do apostems grow in the throat except for the two tongs, so take them out in the same manner as the two tongs.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was lodged within her throat, namely a small abscess; and it had almost completely closed off her entire throat, such that the woman could not breathe due to the swelling that was occurring, and could neither eat nor drink, and died if she remained in this state for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had been pierced with two needles through both nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore quickly pierced it with a needle on one side, then removed the pus through the other nostril, and a large portion of the abscess; then I pierced the other nostril with another needle, and held the mouth open and pressed down her tongue; afterward I pierced the needle into these abscesses, and scooped out a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus the woman's throat was relieved, and she began to drink water and wine, and did not stop cutting away at this abscess for a long time; the abscess grew again and filled up the space that I had previously emptied, until it became very large; then I pushed it out through her mouth and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it did not grow back; and I left these parts and only God knows what happened to them afterward.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When referring to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not very large and round, it is called "uve".
