Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not improve much, and you see that the pus has subsided, and it is thin, then you should drain it; and if it is round and not very long, and it is bloody or dark red, then you should avoid incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger from the pain.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	When you see it, according to the method that I have mentioned, of its size and length, that you make the pain sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the tool that we have recalled before; then put the needle in the eye, and pull it out, and cover it with one or two of the tools that I have mentioned in the incision of the two mandrakes.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the superfluity that is outside the natural term; for if you cover more, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two mandrakes, and cure it until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pain is too great for the patient to bear, then it is necessary to use a needle for cauterization of the sensitive area.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cauterization is sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the pain puts his head on the clean surface, and then presses the tongue against the instrument that we have said or chapter of cauterization, and confines with sharp and live fire, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and in using this movement of the instrument, from which is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the head has a hair or put the medicine, like the movements of a spoon, and puts the instrument on all the medicine above the uvula; and the pain lies on his chest, so that the saliva and muscle secretion from his mouth of the medicine insides, so that it does not fall to the throat and the blood; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press on the uvula, the quantity of half an hour, until you see the relief and the medication of the medicine is calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wipe the cotton in the medicine, and squeeze the instrument to all the cotton on the uvula; and do this often, until the cauterization of the medicine is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five days. And if you have the task of restarting the cauterization of the medicine, then restart it, and after the cauterization stitch around the uvula, with cotton in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be arosed by sharp cold, and be cured of garglings as long as they are healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more reliable with incision than with cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take sage and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and veronica and similar herbs, and all or some of them in a pot, and put honey in it, and let it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot have an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or tin, and one of the prongs is stuck in the patient's mouth until the steam rises to the wound through the nose, until the wound is dead; afterwards, it is often repeated until the wound dries, and make sure you do not make steam at the beginning of the appearance of the abscess, for many things happen; and do not make steam except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If this instrument is not present, take a cloth and put it inside the head to cover the mouth so that the steam does not irritate the mouth; for the cloth does not cause harm to the mouth, and it is good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often it is necessary to remove objects such as bones or fish spines from the throat, or nothing at all; therefore, you should remove what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun at all times with the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and what does not open and is returned to the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit the object as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if the object is forced out by vomiting; or the object swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to the thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes back to the throat, it will be removed, and then draw out the instrument; and if it does not come out as we have said, then use the instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the curved instruments be bent to the head so that they can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high; and watch that you do not touch the epiglottis, that nothing comes into it, nor push the bone in; and it is better that the hairs push the instrument, for it is more likely that the thing is as such; if the pushing goes down, or it pulls the instrument all the way out, evenly, until it is fully out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat suture
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no suture of the throat, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and if it does not help, then look at the throat of the hairs to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the shoe, then trace it with a small needle, or with fine needles that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it does not work, then take a hair-like needle, and push it into the throat of the patient, then push or move the needle through the flesh, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the wounds are too painful all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take plenty of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in the direction of swallowing, and move it to their hand often; and as soon as the shoe feels the cold, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not smell as we have said, of sulfur, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the grape, do this many times, for it will not disappear quickly.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of the fumigation is that you hold the pot or where there is charcoal visible, and place a cloth cover on it in the middle, and in that puncture the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and put the head of the cane in their mouth, and close the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes through the nose; and the nose will now clear, and if it does not, start the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink any vinegar; and then the matter is that it should go through this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the throat, so that when it can be seen, it resembles curved needles to enter the throat; and it has the shape of a beak, and it has roughness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot slip.
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what memory comes after one and another in this book, and they differ in puncturing and cutting; and it is in two ways that the one is in its own shape, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the limbs when they are at the chest.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the main type are different from those that come from the base, and the abscesses of the neck are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if abscesses are to be not pierced until the swelling is completed; and if of such that it is necessary to pierce when they are crusty, and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beyond joints, and it is left until it is swollen inside, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is located near the main limb, and if you delay puncturing it until it dies, it will harm the main limb; or if it is located near the base, if you puncture it too late, it will not be able to heal properly, and will remain open and infected for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is best to clean the wound of the abscess puncture according to its completion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of the fever, and the reduction of the pain and inflammation, and the relief of the main symptoms of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is best to make the puncture where the abscess is most dependent on the body, and where it opens most easily; and let the puncture be long and straight, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, nerves, and arteries, and in all cases where there is no bleeding.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In such cases, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the gut, it is better to leave the puncture until it has healed and completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it beforehand, the blood from it will flow along with the veins, and it is full of filth; and by chance they harden the lips and pierce through it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is punctured according to the wide vein, as the member has need of it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary to re-sew small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many wounds according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if such abscesses or it is necessary to cover the cure, and cover; when it has become as soft as cloth, and is dead, then it should be done as one does with bubbles: and if such abscesses are cut in three angles, and if such abscesses are covered like the fleece of wool, as abscesses of arrows; and if such abscesses or you make a round shape, and other shapes and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who do not have a head, if the pustule is superficial, it is necessary to lance it plainly; and when the pustule is large, and has a great boil, and you lance it, do not draw out all the boil in that hour, but take a part; then stop the pustule the next day, then take nothing else; do this by many times of great and great, until the boil is all out; especially if the evils are of weak virtue, or women carrying, or small children, or old infirm.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Because the experienced never trust with the outflow of the boil, that by chance the evils die, and you do not lose.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, dry the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if a tailor complains, mitigate with tent of linen or wool cotton; and if there are large abscesses, and there is much pus, it is necessary that you stuff each one with an envelope so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have twisted it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shreds of linen to avoid moisture, and bind it to the skin; then open, and treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, apply sharp cold and cooling, and wipe the cloth, and place it on the affected area for many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply government and treatment, and the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is very tense, and if the wound or abscess is very nervous, it is recommended that you place tents and moistened cloths with wine and oil; and if it is in an estate, and the wound is charred, it is recommended that you place moistened cloths with vinegar and oil, or with wine and oil, as we have said; then drain the abscess, dress it, and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or when small abscesses come from the chief, and there are ways that are in cloths, such as the lance of a goose, and very much like that.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also fat and such abscesses that have moisture like chickens; and if there are some that are hard and rough to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not contradict.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the abdomen are such that you should try out all the tools called "entromissoire," which is shaped like this: a thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, it makes it from above down long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off any hair that contains that moisture, for it will remain in place if you leave anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian oil, if present; otherwise, use vinegar and salt, and apply to the wound, and leave it there the next day; and this will continue what is left overnight.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, as before, the second day, and the third, and the fourth, until you are sure that it will not remain overnight; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is not too large, cut it open along this form, from long to short; and pour in your pus, and scrape off all the skin, and put all your care into drawing out the pus from where it is. And if the artery opposes you, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same if it is pus-filled, and cut and treat as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And above the abscess, if it is moist and filled with pus, it is lighter, for it contains little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or boils have no moisture, and are like the ones I copied from an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard and rough and white as a stone, and could not break it; and if one had tried to cut it, they would have made just as bad a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or from the base of the ears, the opening should always be made at the lowest point, to let out the pus; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of goiters
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times there are abscesses at the neck, and they open the jaws, and they become swollen, and sometimes they come from other parts of the body, and they are very painful, and they are intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each goiter is properly within its side, like the neck and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these goiters are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are malignant and do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then which you see of good disposition in the throat, and is similar to the color of the heart, and moves from each part and is not attached to the nerve or artery or conduit, and is not deeply rooted; if it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape every part, and stretch the two lips of the mouth as in opening, if you have skill, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and draw it out slowly and surely, and be careful not to cut the nerve or vein, that the hand does not slip, and do not look too soon, before you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to open it, put vinegar or some powders that stop bleeding into the wound, and close the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is softened, and then begin to poultice.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleaned, return to your work, as long as you complete it; then ask your judge if there are any small scabs remaining, and cut and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the base of the scab, it is not advisable to cut that scab at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you have removed the entire scab, it is necessary that you gather the two lips of the wound and hold them together, then because there is no excess left due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you cover the root of it and pull out the pus, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scabs that have excess left, pierce where it opens and dies; and pierce thus as the one previously said, depending, then apply bandages and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well dressed, if the cure of ointment encouraging char, until they are healed.
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and said of the throat-cutter; but I never saw one in our land, and this is their written account.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the edge of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be avoided; and this cannot be helped because all the veins and the mouth of the evil are in those who have abscesses high in the mouth, or in the throat or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the mouth of the evil, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it out in three circles or four, with a small cut across between the two circles or by the amount of the cut through the soft tissue, not into the cartilage; and those cuts are suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no danger, and the vessels are long and can be tied.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is not afraid, then it is necessary to stretch the skin of the neck all around, then cut the throat until it reaches the windpipe; avoid the blood vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cover the wound as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the stream of the windpipe that jumped through the bone that was broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which we doubt strangulation, gather the two lips of the wound together, and hold them all in place without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause the birth of heat, until they are healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this as long as the throat is completely stiff, and the hairs are judged to be dead, and the defect does not return.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then one should remove the epiglottis for this reason that the hairs cannot remain, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and because they commanded the ancients to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease had passed, and it had passed in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew the wound and cure, as long as it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife, and stabbed herself in the throat, and cut part of her windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not bled much from the vein, the blood was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and she did not die, but only lost her voice, and returned to her usual state; because I know that there is no fear in the healer of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of a yolk, and is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; or naturally, without cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental way is in two ways, one of which is similar to a large goiter, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us through an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be opened except by a small incision in the chest, and the proof and search are made throughout the neck: if you find it as in a large goiter, and cannot be removed at all, if it covers, as one covers a large goiter, and remove it completely, if there is none; and search well and treat it as necessary until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	The fire cautery in
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways we have, and I will tell you all the similarities; but now it is necessary for me to say all the difference between us and the issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the issue is cold and fever-causing, until the boils have passed, and it is accompanied by the purgation; then the fever and the cold rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With our way, there is neither cold nor fever nor pain, and it contains the syphilitic pustule, which is its own disease and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a small boil, and becomes large; and they are similar in two ways, either dry or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When coming to the care of a new patient, it is necessary to first test and inquire about the instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form as described in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method for inquiring about abscesses is that you press or slightly wet the finger that you will use to probe into the abscess, and gradually return it, until you know that the instrument has reached the core, according to the size of the abscess; then remove the entromissoire, and be careful not to let it slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the running wound is red in color, make it as I have described for other abscesses; and if after using the entromissoire there is no more running, know that it is thick, then cut it in a cross shape, and take pincers, and scrape lightly from every part and remove the cloth where it lies, that you may take it out with the new patient; and if you cannot take it out whole, then tear it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If nothing remains, it returns to us many times; and if it lingers a little, and does not bother you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, keep the wound clean, and apply soothing remedies to the abscess, and treat other cures until it is healed; and if it is great, cut off both lips of the wound, and treat what remains with char.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if it continues to beat against you or other things, and hurries you, apply the broken glass of vitriol to the wound, and let it remain for two or three days until the wound heals, and rest the abscess of the blood; then return to cover what remains of the wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the instruments used for extracting stones, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albarret", and one that is called "breb", and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to extract the stones of fistulas; and they are also like the needles that one uses for sewing, and they are made of gold, or iron, or silver, and they cost as much as those that are already yellow, and they are more useful for extracting the splinters of fistulas; and they are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the fistulas.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the nails are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are nails that have two thorns in three ways; and if there are nails that have three thorns, and are also in three ways; and if there are nails that have two thorns, and a single thorn nail, and are also in three ways; and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these that are used to make them are sharp, and there are some that do not cut except from one part, from which we remove the skin, because they do not cut the vein or the nerve; and of these intruments are the needles placed in sheaths, so that the pain does not persist at the opening of the abscesses; and there are three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one never uses more than one sharp instrument like this, except in the hollow parts, such as legs, arms, and breasts, and in similar places.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is never placed back into the joint that should be aligned with veins, and arteries, and always returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of some men when they begin to rot, as they seem like breasts of women; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, should follow this form of this line b. until g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine mixed with charcoal, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast sinks down, and is softened by its great size like in women, then make it into two pieces above, by similar cuts; so that one holds to the other at the end of each, so that the largest line contains the smallest according to this form, from this line b. to the line g.; then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not made completely, because the pains do not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with cotton moistened in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it melts the remaining fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the knees
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the knees are ways of hard scrofula when there are lumps, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the cavity that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply old cotton to the wound, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.

And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, then make an incision as we have said for cutting into scrofula, and if the wound opens again, then cauterize as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the tearing of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is torn, and the flesh above is hardened, then often abscesses form, and also blood and pus flow; and if you know it is for the artery, then make an incision long and parallel; and when you feel it with your fingers, it is stretched; and if it is for the vein, then make a long incision below; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is outside of the bones and angles and neck and mouth of other wounds, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to use the iron cautery, and the one who is at the head should also use it, and in the one who is swollen due to an artery bleeding through the long skin; then open the belly as much as possible, and tear the artery from the cloth until it is exposed; then remove one needle, and pierce the other on the other side of the rib, and hold the artery with a double thread in II loops, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then do not remove the flesh that is between the two ribs of an intercostal until the pus that is inside is removed, and remove the abscess; then remedy the care that has been injured, as long as the rib is healed; then cure what is related to ointment for this, as long as it is healthy; and if the abscess is in the belly of the vein, if you dip your hand in the pus that comes from the abscess to all the skin, then remove the needle from the hand that you hold, and pierce it, and there should be a double thread, so that you can pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have told you, or the thread of one of the two parts of the question as the thread of the first needle; and if you doubt that the thread will not hold, then remove another needle from all the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four loops; then cover the abscess until the excess is removed, then cover the excess of the wound and leave what is attached; then put a piece of moist linen cloth in wine and oil, then remedy the care of tents and ointments until it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses also come to the neck when it is cut, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And they often occur in the helpers and the doors and in all the places where there are joints, and that is very painful, and its color resembles the color of the blood, and it is in many different positions with pain; and when it is stretched, it causes great pain, and does not remain in place, but outside the skin; and it moves from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, or outside or above, and those who are in the joints do not need to cover with iron: perhaps they cause contraction; and those who are at the top or front, make the skin thin.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if it has a point to a needle, and the copper at its root; and if it is large, if it hangs by the tip, and the skin, then the bone and assemble the wound at the seam, and the cure until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large swellings hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There is never any in the belly and not in other parts of the body, and it is a disease called "funge" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has a subtle root, and large and small; and I saw the man who had two or bellies that were more like funges than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thin root, and they were torn, and they bled with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one XVIII ounces heavy, and in the other VI З., and the works in the incision is that you look if the hairs are moist, and the color of the arrow is white and moist and of subtle root; if the copper has a wide spatula, and they are in your presence the fire cauterization.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting often comes too great damage of blood, and if you see the hair is spouting and dangerous from the incision of the iron, then take the thread of good quality, and tie the arrow as we have said, and leave it II hours; then restrain, and do not cease to pull the thread of good quality until it copes the arrow, and cut through it with work; and if the roots are large, then use the copper itself for the belly, but you must well copper the other half, then cauterize that it does not revisit; then care for the wound, and guard that you do not copper the thread which is of pale color and poor sense and of lait regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these infected abscesses, and I will come to treat sores like this afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the shoulder is bruised
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the bruise comes from fire wound or cut of the gangrene, and is above the belly and in some of the sores, as it has in other wounds, of blood which cut veins or arteries according to what is before, or of swelling; and if it is from the cut of the gangrene and from the issue of the pus, then the color of the abscess is like the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.
