Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when one presses it with their hand, do not force much; and if it is due to arrows, it is large and hard, and is like a pustule in quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the signs are that you look to see if it is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave, let the care be done by someone else.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often doubt and fear, such as I have told you about abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bladder, it is necessary to command the patient to dye his clothes, and be extended straight out, then seize all around the belly; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the limb that you have designated as the great sinew; then extend half of the abscess above all the large sinew; then tie it tightly with a strong silk cord, and so be the other half of the abscess lying flat; then cut through the skin, and withdraw the intestine; if you pierce the great sinew, remove it, and draw out the intestine from behind the belly; and if you pierce the bladder, take it at the base, and cop the excess; and if the artery makes you go against it, or the vein, go around it slowly, then return to your work and take two needles, and cut off two pieces of thread, and cut through the skin as you have done before; then pierce the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the limb as long as it can bear, and let the dead flesh die by itself; or you take it when it has become thin and ready to die, then treat the limb as we have said; and strain out the pus or moisture that you find, then treat the limb as it needs, and soak the limb.
dou chancre	For the fire cautery, instruct
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have mentioned in the division the similarities of chancre, and how to treat it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancre occurs in the mouth, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancient one says that when chancre is in a place where it can be removed as if it were chancre which is in mammary glands, and in the breasts, and in similar places, and it should all be removed when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, if it does not matter that you approach it, for I have never been able to cure any of them; and no one has ever cured any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the surgeries, when it is in the place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you remove once the pain of black bile; then clean it if it has obvious repletion, then wipe the pain on good flesh to do the surgery; then pour your instruments or poison, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow fully, and well wipe the wound with your hand or something, and if the bleeding does not stop, it is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, so cauterize until the blood is stopped; then treat other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the previous division the similarities of dropsy, and how the assembly of the swelling is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is only swollen; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarche, for it is a fatal thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called «eclites» by medicines, and the cure does not work, if you look at whether the pains are weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, as all and solution of vomiting and similar things; then do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great virtue, and he has no other disease except dropsy alone, and he is not too young nor too old, then thus proceed: raise the patient upright over your hands, and the assistants press the belly pushing the swelling to the lowest part of the worst, then take the spatula in this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And cutting at the tip, and ensure that no part is too thin so that it can reach the intestines when thrown, and cannot be bleached; then check if there is hydrops towards the intestines: if it is necessary to make an incision III dozen straight down from the side of the belly; and if it is for the liver disease, then your cut should be on the left side of the belly III dozen; and if it is for the mucus, then it should be on the right, and it is not necessary that the hairs grow over the cut so that the excess does not run to the weakest limb; then pierce the skin with the instrument, and push, and lift your hand from all the space between the skin and the stomach as if scraping at the quantity of an angle or around; then pierce the stomach until the space reaches the desired length, and this is the legs of the needle, then remove it, and it is bent in this instrument with which this is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and it is of light rain or light rust, and it has a small puncture on its part; and it costs one third on one side, two on another side, and one on the other; and it is the same as the one that is cut as a pen, and it is the form of the incision that the scribes make the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of the instrument is the alarm, so that when the instrument comes to the tip, if you draw it now above the instrument; voiding the half or the third part, because if you void more than it should be in that hour, by chance if the pain dies from the resolution of its spirit of the arm, or it hits palm, or it approaches to death; but in voiding according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the pain mean, and its pricks; then remove the instrument and retain the tip, and it is retained now for the one who pierces the puncture that is above the tongue, of which I have spoken, that you perforate in this manner; then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the pain suffering thus, and take a small quantity from the tip; do this every day, and guard yourself from following as long as it does not delay but a little bit of the tip.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt the pain and leave it for a long time, the cure of the sepulture or sandbath, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and if it is tainted with drinking; and the cure of desiccative medicines as long as it is healthy, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the sharp object, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the removal of the staff
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever is born without a sharp object in the staff, or the sharp object is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to prick quickly, do not pierce at all points with great subtlety according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or puncture the subtle needle deeply, and hold it and him thus three times or four, and when he wants to make urine, if it is not convenient, for the urine that comes forth does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is punctured is small, it is treated with a subtle needle as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the puncture in their own flesh are blinded, for no one is born with the puncture at the top of the staff, because they cannot urinate before they leave their staff high; and they cannot urinate because the matter cannot come to the marrows, and it is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the hairs lie evenly on their backs, the head of the knife and the coping are as wide as the tail of a quill, so that when the puncture is made in the middle, it is done as it should be; and guard against bleeding which often comes, and if it does, stanch the blood with the same liquid that stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the knife
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	often come worms in the knife, and it is an ugly appearance; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; if you should prick them with a fine needle, and cut and clean all of them, then put on moist cotton bandage; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wound is malignant, with a putrid color and foul smell, then you must cauterize it with fire.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cleaned it, and if the wound is deep into the flesh and partly inside the skin and partly outside, then you must first remove the part that is inside; and when it is clean, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, do not be sure that the arrowhead is not piercing, and if it becomes black and corrupt inside and at its base; then remove everything that is black and corrupted, then apply a poultice made of honey and flour mixed with ground peach and almond kernels, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if there is a flow of blood, then treat the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries aid in two dispositions together: that is, at the flow of blood and at corruption; and if the patient's penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to apply a cloth soaked in piss to the wounds and urinate on them; and when the skin has erupted at the head of the staff that has not yet been circumcised, or for a wound or abscess, then it is necessary to scorch it with the instrument of hair, until the flesh is separated, and deliver the patient from all parts of the staff; and if it is a difficult matter to devise this cure, then it is necessary to scorch it at the head of the staff and the skin, and apply a subtle cloth of moist linen, cold, so that it does not erupt again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not different from other wounds; therefore, when we perform this work of our will, and properly with children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the least harmful to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not direct circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen the greatest part of the masters and the wise men who performed circumcision around the time of the Deluge, and at all ages; if it was the best because it had two layers, and perhaps if one coped with the other above and delayed the other below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is prolonged, and the pain is doubled, and the wound healing which is done with the point of a member is not assured; and the healing of the wound by chance may escape the iron, and corrupt the work, and many times it happens that they are born in such a way that they have no need of healing and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the wound healing which is done with force throughout the entire length of the thread, I have found the best of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally throughout the entire length; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and in the manner of the first work is that you make the child think that you are only tying the thread around the stick as much as possible, and then throw the force between your hands or away from your feet so that the child does not see it, nor any of the instruments; then close your hand around the stick and blow gently, and take it up as high as the part of the stick is whole; then clean the dirt that is gathered there, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie the other end to the other thread; and hold the two threads together with the second piece of cloth and the index finger, and press between the two threads, then lift the force gently and take the head of the stick; then let the blood flow little by little, for it is the most dangerous; and put powder on top and on top of the powder a plaster made from a piece of raw fat cooked with rose water, confit with rose oil and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and cure the other wound as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of forces for the mummification is as follows: the two heads should be tight and sharp, and the two hands should be equally large.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of mummification is when the knife is too short for the incision; therefore, you should extend it to your elbow, and similarly, the copper, and if you cannot hold it at your elbow, then use tongs and then the copper.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they have passed three hours, and what is outside the rod is swollen, let it remain until the abscesses are calm, and scrape lightly; and if the copper, as you can move it, and keep it away from the part of the rod, it will not harm them.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the limb of things that are dirty wounds from powder, which we have said or treated for powders, and if you exceed measure, it will not harm; therefore, treat as we have said until they are healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Retention of urine is due to obstruction of the stone, or of blood congealed, or of bowel, or of a charred, or of similar things, which we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention by the stone which is hanging or collapsing the bladder, then it is necessary to raise the legs above the back, and put the feet on the back, and extend the belly from the part above the back, and restrain the legs as much as possible; and therefore, the neck of the bladder is pressed against the stone above, for which reason the urine is released, and if it does not come, as we have said, and the legs feel great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called «siringue», of which this is the form: and it should be made of thin silver wire, like the quill of an egg; and it should be made of a palm length and half, and it should be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie the head of the thread to the top of a piece of wool or cotton, and bore the head of the thread into the tube; and wrap the excess wool and bore it at the head of the tube, then oil the tube with oil or butter and eggs, and make the patient sit on a stool, and the urine and the cloth moistened with warm oil and olive oil and vinegar; then put the tube lightly in the cloth, until it reaches the root of the cloth, then double the cloth over towards the bottom; then bore the tube forward just before the cloth, and the patient feels the urine coming near the empty thing, and this is not made according to this order except for the reason that the conductor or she goes is twisted; then stretch the thread all along the wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it forcefully, and correct the urine; and repeat the tube until the bladder is empty and aligned with the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scarabs or blood come into the bladder, and putrefaction is present, and you see it dripping watery and medicinal substances, then use any instrument called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the threads are passed through it so that the medicine can penetrate well to the end of the catheter, so that the moisture can be drawn out, and put back when necessary; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, place the tip of the catheter in the moisture, and pull the tube out; then draw the moisture into the catheter, and plug it strongly; then the moisture will enter the catheter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster which is used to clysterize the bladder: it is thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie. de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken in the section about stones, and their extraction together with medicines; and I have mentioned the difference between a stone in the rain, and all the signs, and which kind of stone one should open with an incision; and in the bladder, and in the staff; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder occurs more often in children, and this is a sign that the sharp pain of the bladder, like a sharp sting in its subtlety; and it opens hair, and gives great pain to the staff, and can happen many times, and then it returns; and at too many of these jumps, the foundations; and it is light to the healing of children up to the age of four, and is very painful in old people, and is constant in those between middle age and old age; and it is a lighter cure for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with a poultice, to draw out all the matter that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never clogs when seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound by the feet, and make it stand upright and move away from the opening, so that the stone descends to the edge of the bladder, and does not once rise above the thigh; then place it between your hands and clean it, with your hands away from your thighs, so that the bladder is completely drained below; then grasp and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut across the stone.

Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be made larger, and a larger wound should be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor. de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is hardly any stone in women, and if it ever happens, the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-knowing who will undress herself, specifically when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well versed in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that if the woman's stone is larger than the man's, it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear involved. And if necessary, it is necessary to grab a woman who is very skilled, and point out where the truth lies, and if you do not find it, then it is necessary to use a very subtle mirror; and present a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command of the examination of the stone; and look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: therefore it is necessary to put her hand on her belly and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, she must hold her hand outside her belly, and recommend that she put her hand on her belly and press firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. And in all ways that you can, until you remove everything; and guard that the blade does not touch the bone; and make sure this work is safer; and keep from bleeding, and make sure the incision does not become infected; and if anything goes against you, such as an abscess or bleeding or infection, cure what goes against you according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the wound is painful and does not want to undergo this work due to its horror, then use perforation, as I have told you, and it is that when you are sure by the signs that we have said that the sharp object is in, then sit the wound on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess at the part farthest from everything wide, and place the perforation down the long axis of the body; and make it wide enough so that all the sharp object comes out, then put cotton on the wound, and tie it, and let the remaining sharp object drain, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the sharp object to come out of the wound mouth, then you must insert a pen or the instrument used to remove the sharp object from hydropiques, because its form is as before; and enlarge the wound slightly, and make sure the sharp object returns, and is assembled after six months or within a year, and when it is assembled as before, and so on the sharp object will pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	of abscesses of the joints
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	There are many positions in this section of the branch that cause fear to many, which seems to me to be better left alone; and I will tell you about the work and similar things of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come from wounds and immediately to joints; and this is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know from excessive sharp and cold, which is spread in joints, or from impact; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the wound; and it does not cause pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and perhaps some greyish, pus-filled, and foul-colored abscesses come from a vein or an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, it is known by the position of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and you should only touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of opening a vein is known by its position at the expression of gentle touching with the fingers, and can well make the incision on this resemblance, and on the other parts; and you should cover the wounds, then the wound in the top, and the tail of the white fac, and deliver the suspensoire from all parts of the wound.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is already sewn with these needles, then you should make the incision, and cover; and if it is in the white fac, or in what is inside the vessels, then you should deliver all that is held, and cover it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the arrow's head is behind the shoulder, then it is necessary to cut off everything, and extract the arrow, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your surgeries are completed, apply the wound with a soft cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess surrounded by a pus-like envelope, with the softening of the groin, and the pain is severe when it moves; and the treatment of this disease is just as difficult and dangerous as the previous one, and we will tell you about its surgery, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to seat the misaligned joint on its proper seat, then lift the suspensor muscles with your fingers to the verge of the tendons, and stretch them evenly; then cut the spatula widely across the traversing part of the tendons, until they are exposed, and then scrape each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples; then take a needle or double thread, and tie it to the first limb where the blood came from, and tie it to the other end; then stitch them straight in the middle, according to the length of the body, and cut the corrupted veins; then cure the wound as in the others, so that none of the tendons are damaged; for by this no harm comes, and if the blood comes from all the tendons, it is necessary to remove the tendons from all the tendons; so that the joint does not lose its norrissement through the incision of the tendons, and they dry and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this branch are by the section that comes out from the toothache, or the extension over the belly in the part of the gums, because the intestines descend from that section to one of the sides; and this toothache is either from the section itself, or from the extension of it, and these two methods of many causes are: by percussion, or jumping, or shouting, or lifting heavy weight, and similar things; and the signs when it is the extension of the toothache, is that it is little and little, in long tension, and does not come suddenly; and it is the abscesses equal up to the jaw, because the tooth is close to the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs of a sudden gum cut, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and has various abscess appearances, outside the skin, and it is for the end of the intestine and the heart after the cut of the gum.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never the intestines with the worms, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer from the wound, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments of fear, for which it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the way of the work is that you command or let the wound open inside the intestine with your hand, if it can be pulled out; then place the curved part of a spoon over his neck between your hands, and loosen the jaws; then place the crown of the spoon above, and cover all the skin of the belly with oil; then put your index finger in the opening of the wound, in the place where the intestine is between the white gum that is outside the skin of the belly, and between the second gum, and behind the belly, and between the second gum; and push the white gum up with your left hand, and loosen the belly to all the gum; and command the assistant to stretch the belly up, and remove what is behind the skin; and if you find anything, if you find any intestine or white gum hard, and if you find anything, put it in the stomach outside; then take a needle or a thick thread made of 12 threads, and put it in the back part of the gum, which is after the skin of the belly; then cover the threads with oil, and tie them together in the form of a cross, and fasten the gum, which we have said is outside the skin of the belly, with a strong thread of 2 parts; then cover the threads with oil, and tie them together in 2 parts, so that none of the vessels that grow there can enter into wounds, that aposteme does not come; and finally put the first thread according to the first thread, and after these two threads leave the gum which is outside the belly the great of one finger; and then the other according to the roundness that the belly carries; then cover in the part which is outside the skin of the belly, as we have said before; then moisten linen with oil, and put it on the wounds, and moisten the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white swelling that we have mentioned after incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and leave the wound as it heals through him; and if it takes a long time to settle, then roast with sharp hot iron, and put on what we have said, until it heals; then treat the wound with other treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia, carnal
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done as in the branch that is together with the viscera, in a manner that you tie the veins, after the groin slightly open; then cover it, and treat the abscess of what works, until the veins heal; and the treatment as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never does the rip occur due to anger and opening the wounds; and no one should pull out any of the intestines from the wounds, and if they do, it is rare, and they should be repaired every hour; and in any case, if it remains too long at this point, the wound or the abscess believes that the intestine is being pulled out; and this happens due to the extension of the syphac which is at the rip, as we have said, because it is stretched, then it is softened and inflated the wound and opened; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have previously said; and never is the cure done in this way: and it is that the painful parts are laid on top of their back between your hands, then cover the wound of the rip enflated with a large cloth according to the quantity of three fingers; and then pull out the syphac which is outside the skin that covers it, then take the knife and put it on top of the wound of the syphac; and press against the front of the belly, then cut the two wounds above the head of the knife, and both; then pull out the head of the knife, and do not cover the syphac or stretch the belly or anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the intestines; then cure by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the strings, if you defend and heal the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sutures are tight, and do not appear in the tear, and the cauterization is silent in this place, and more likely to save.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the shoes
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the leather of the shoes is softened in some men, because the charred parts inside are softened, and it can be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened leather over the natural leather; then gather the two lips to one seam, and if you see, first remove the excess softened leather at three or four seams; then stitch between the seams, and cure as with other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	with great care
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	It is not proper to speak of cauterization in our law, and therefore I do not wish to mention it in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: one is that the patient should respond with cauterization when asked, and be cured by cauterization; and the other is because we often have to use cauterization on some animals to help us, such as a goat and a sheep and a pig and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cauterization is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, make the animal sit in high heat, until the hairs are softened and while they are still hot; then take them in your hand, until they are returned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the proper treatment of the waist: it is necessary to tie the beast, and press the leather of the codpieces with your right hand, then hang the suspensor, and cope over each eye at the cop, when you have them well cauterized; and leave no pore of the sensitive skin and the subtle skin that is on the vessels; and this method of cauterization is milder than that made by attraction, for the reason that by attraction something of the codpieces remains, by which the beast desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	des hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermofrodie is according to two methods among men: one is that between the two legs open wide as the figure of a woman's nature, with hair, and sometimes cutting the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is in women, and has above the penis like a penis and two legs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of the male and female is that you cut off all the foreskin stumps, and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, of men whose urine sprays through the skin of the legs, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a device placed above the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have had it as big as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to clean the excess of the tentigene with your hand or a cloth, and wipe it lightly; and do not move too much, as there is no blood coming out, until the other cure is healed; and for another char that is born at the mouth of the marsh, and use it, and perhaps it will jump out, and it is according to the appearance of a cow, and because of this they called the old "cowdisease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to perform the procedure as we have described the traction, and care until it is healed.
de erratique	of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perfectly known, or the cause is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come, or it is caused by artificial means, such as a sharp needle or subtle suture, and it is made in the marriage bed, or in the cost, or elsewhere, and they do not conceive, and pregnancy, and possibly the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the appearance of the baby.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears near the surface, it is best to apply your two fingers or a spoon.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle swelling under the lips, and it is near the surface, then hasten, and do as follows: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, with her legs spread; then stretch the lips forming a tube, until the subtle swelling is drawn out, and is over the swelling; then take linen, and dip it in oil, and place it on the limb, and bind the woman to a bed every day, so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and sharp, it is necessary to apply a poultice similar to a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from a horse bite, hang it up and cover it with a cloth; and have the medicines steeped in blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and abundant wine; then apply a large piece of wet plaster, so that the wound cannot heal; and thus keep it long, and then cover it with a dry linen tent; then treat other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the horse bite occurs in the marsh, cover it according to this method, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that forms in the marsh should not be touched with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually bleed, and when the hemorrhoids become old, they become thrombosed; and we have already said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and thromboses, when they are newly formed in the marsh, and do not appear until felt, are not treated by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that can be felt at the edge of the marsh are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, it is necessary to put the woman in a cold house, then stretch the thrombus with tongs, and cut off its roots, then powder medicines that stop bleeding such as acacia and sulfur and incense and similar things; then bathe her feet at the door for an hour, then put her in very cold water; if blood comes out, sit her in a decoction of sumac and skin of green apples and gall and similar things, and then take wheat flour, and knead it with honey and oil, and make a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he is sated, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him inhale smoke through his back and breasts without causing injury; then take the limb, and soak it in juice of plantain or of agrimony with old wine, and make him inhale the smoke on the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ready to burst, treat the limb with poultices until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, and resembles a sharp thorn, if it should cover it as I have said of the thelul; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses from the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come from the marsh, such as chancre and pustular abscess and herpes and esthenia and fistulas and hemorrhoids and pustular abscess chaut, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary to tell in this treatment of the abscess chaut that comes from the marsh, which is not one of the abscesses that come together; and if you know how to use the iron, look at whether the abscess is agus at the beginning of its appearance, and with fever and heat, and if it becomes red, then see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce, but make it wait as long as the pain is eased; and then place the sore on its seat, and have two small seats where it bends, and lean against its back and gather its feet at the parts beyond the leg; and let its knees be spread, and put its arms away from its hips, and tie them firmly with a good bandage; then apply the splint to the left side of the body, and make it comfortable; and when you see this instrument being applied, that you check the depth of the wound, so that what comes out of the instrument does not go further than it should, and does not cause the sore to bleed; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it is necessary to put the horn of the instrument on top, and stain the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the abscess is opened and they do it by hand, if it needs to be covered at the head, cover it with spatumile leat; and when the boil is emptied, it is necessary to put in the wound thin tents soaked in rose oil or green dry oil; and place the tent from the wound to the edge of the marsh, and place above the marsh and above the other clean thin tents soaked in hot water; then after two hours of ointment applying to it, as long as it is healed; and never lift the marsh and the wound by a poultice of hot water and honey, and then of hot water or roots of lis and aristolochia are cooked; then reapply the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is stitched in the marsh, it is necessary to avoid cooking with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	at birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The midwife is first to the birth that she knows the figure of the natural childbirth, and the signs as you see the woman approaching, and desires to smell the ar: then hasten the child to come out; then cleanse that child according to the natural figure, and it is the issue with its head, and the second with him; and when you see these signs, if it is necessary to press lightly on his belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when he goes up to his head, it is the second with him, and it is washed in the marsh of its superfluities by good cleaning; and this that comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It never comes up from its feet, and it comes far from the body or the back, and the hands, or it comes up its belly, or sometimes, and is twisted by chance onto its neck, and by other bad figures; if there is need to correct this matter, the midwife should be skilled and subtle in these things, and if she errs and is deceived, I will show you all the figures how one must help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes up its head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth with great pain, and her strength is weak, then let the midwife sit on a stool, or the women hold her; and apply oil or fenugreek that has been cooked to it, and then give the midwife a small spatula of this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and pierce the second joint, and cover its angle as far as the moisture that is now corrected; and take the belly of the woman so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to smear the woman with fenugreek powder mixed with mustard oil; then let her inhale and expectorate the condition, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if this now causes the child to descend.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are dislocated, it is necessary to gently and gradually reset them; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet high; then remove the chair from the ground, and tie the woman, so that she does not fall during the removal; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cover the hands with the cloth that was previously placed there, extract the child, and gently reset it.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's feet above
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on its feet, if it is necessary to place it above; then gradually turn it and extend it little by little until it is even; then grasp both feet and extend them gradually.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up quickly, command it to hold still, and make it sneeze from the condition; if it jumps away, then God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump away as we have said, then gradually turn it and extend it until it is in accordance with the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is certainly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	If it does not come out as we have said, take muscle powder of high altitude, and oil of wormwood, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in a high chair until above the ribs; and when she is softened above, make her a garland of mint, and put it on her, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her spit and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child has just come out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's knees above
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.
