When the child comes in this form, so put your hands gently and gently on it; then lean it on its back, and hang its feet down, and let it lie on the bed; and gently fold your hands, and then take its hands above the belly, and remove the cusses from off, until it is cleaned underneath; and if the child does not move, take its feet and form it gently, then move its belly upwards, then put your hands; and slowly feed the child little by little; and command the woman to wait until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out wide a hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to engineer to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, then lift the woman, and go; if she cannot go, then make her lie on the bed, and bend her legs together; then administer the muscle relaxant that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the chair, then study to bring back the hand; and when the child is according to the natural figure, and make it sneeze, and command her to hold it until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's neck, and let his hands be spread out, and his face turned towards the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the bailer wipe his hand, then turn it slowly and lightly; when it is even, if you put some muscle oil of high and old, as we have said, then command him to move slowly; when you have done this, make him sit on a chair, and command him to bend over; and make him spit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner to all the second one
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to doing this to the second one, if the second one can hold your hand, until the moisture is drained; and if the child can move his face and neck, then hold the baby's head, so it is not held back, and the child dies; then feed the child inside, as you should, and command the woman to bend over once: then let him go lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is often the case that twins are born, and sometimes not at all; and this is not an uncommon thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is strange that they do not live, if not all; I know that they can be multiplied, and are separated by the same sac which gives them birth, which is attached to the placenta; and sometimes they come out naturally as one at a time, just like we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out harshly, as we have said the care should be, and the birth canal is subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do thus as it should be for their health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	There are no children formed in the first through fifth or sixth or seventh or up to fifteen, and all are formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious, and it is necessary that the bath cures all, because by chance similar things happen to him; so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you care for the woman of the dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to do manual work; if the woman is of sound virtue and has no accident or fear of death; then it is necessary that you smear her with a two-part ointment made from the tannin of willows and fenugreek and linseed, then wipe the bath's hands with these oils and muscillages; then lightly apply the ointment to the woman's hands, or wherever it is convenient for her, and if the child has been born and is wrapped in cloths that are not suitable for this, and take care that the child does not descend over its head; then smear the ointment in the child's eyes or on its neck or in its mouth or in its palms or behind its ears or on its forehead or on its chest or between its ribs; and if the child has descended, then smear it with the ointment on its back, and hold the child in your left hand, and apply the ointment to all of its body lightly, and smear the ointment in any of the places we have mentioned, until the thing is empty; and this is the form of the ointment:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then remove the other thorn, where you have the skill, so that the extraction is even; and then place it evenly by moving one part and another, to make it move, and let the thorns be sharp to hold, as in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, use some of its two oils, and drive them into that part, and pull out the other part; and if it does not remain, put this thorn or higher up the limb, and do so until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be returned by tightening, then you must wrap around the cloth, as much as it moves; then cut it at the joint of the foot or at the heel, and thus you should do in the other hand, and so on.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	If the question concerns a child who is large and has a sharp bone at the neck, it is necessary to insert the spatula between your fingers and break the sharp bone; or you can use the tool called "almidach", with which the instruments or chapter that follows this one are made; and in the same way, if the child has a great natural head, draw the bones with pincers, and if the child's neck springs out, hold it firmly until the blood issues; and if it cannot issue, cut it into pieces as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or outside the ribs, it is necessary to pierce it until the blood flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the infant is above its feet, then the traction is light, and the pressure at the mouth of the marsh is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if the infant is stiff in the belly or the foot, it is recommended that you extract it from the wrapped cloth over your hand; and when the belly or the foot is open, as long as the moisture that is there is corrected; and if the other member is broken, and the question remains, then bring the billy goat's hand in front of the marsh, and pull it to the mouth of the marsh; then bring the one or two, and pull it out; and if the mouth of the marsh is retracted by an abscess that has come, it is not recommended to strain, but it is recommended to manage moist and fat things; and the management emplausters, and siece in a high mollifying and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the shoulder is dislocated on its side, and you can put it back in place, as we have said for the living child; and if you cannot do so, then treat it by pieces, and leave nothing of the secondary.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, treat it as we have said for abscesses that come in the marsh; and if blood comes out, it should be tightly bandaged, and treated with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had died, then consulted the other about it, and refused to let the others die.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some abscesses appeared in the groin, and they swelled up so much that they burst, and then began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to the doctor, and after a long time, I thought it was not healing.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong attractive ointment, and some bones were pulled out, and after some time others came out.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound, and through it I saw many bones, until the woman was in much better condition; and she saw the woman like this for a long time, and it was only a little bit of blood from the body; and I do not remember this chapter except that when masters find an unusual thing, they know how to give aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	bring the marble back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	For the form of pressure, we use books; and at two returns to two questions about two joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the corners should be more subtle than the restrictor, and be made of flat or round; and the mouth of the funnel should be two fingers wide, and the edge of the trees should be a palm and a half long; and in the two joints, they should be two supports of this same funnel, which are firmly fixed on one side and the other, half a palm or more long; and these two supports are driven into the mouth of the marble when turning the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of nails; and it has two prongs, as you see, one palm long, and two wide; and when you want to open the mouth all the way with the instrument, place the woman on the bed, the feet together and the legs spread, then push the two prongs together into the mouth, and hold the chief of the instrument between her teeth; then work your hand with the instrument equally, according to the quantity you want to open the mouth of the woman, until the pain makes her do what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all above, and they are multiplied in their similarities; and when the master has them prepared, the more hasty the work, and the higher it is for men due to its quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument because you have not prepared it, for its necessity is not excused.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second instrument is retained at birth, it is necessary to command the hairs that they hold their tails, and then make them expel the conditions, and hold your hands on the mouth and nose; and if they sneeze through there, well enough.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled over the fire; then put a cloth or cover in the pot, and the other head in the mouth of the marsh, and wait until the vapors come into the mouth; then make him spit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint also moves out of place.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains in place after this treatment and is not too strong, command the bath attendant to gently massage her right hand with olive oil or musk mallow, and then put it back in its natural position, and find the second joint; and when she finds it, grasp it and extend it slowly and carefully, so that the marsh does not break during extraction; but it should be gently moved to the right and left, and then removed; if it comes out, it will disappear and dissolve.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the bite of the marsh is extended, we have said the cure of expectoration, and fumigation of herbs; and if she does not have all that we have said, then guard that you do not follow the sucking; but it is advisable that what is at the mouth of the marsh, that you tie to the cheek of the woman, then cleanse with a plaster of quadrifarmaceutic ointment; if she will swallow and return, and it will heal; but nevertheless, when she swallows if there comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and bleeds the pain.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is advisable to use the following fumigations: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to smoke the woman at the retention of flowers and the second ingredient is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like a wire, similar to a needle, and one puts the tip subtly into the nature, and the rest of the wire over the fire; and the smoking is done over the coals, and the lice until they are burned, and then start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not pierced the foundation, but one has stupefied them with some subtle poison: therefore it is necessary for the mother to pierce that poison at its source, and not pierce too deeply, and keep the wound clean; then put on a moist cloth in wine and oil, then the treatment of the wound until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not set, put or press a splint on it, and let it remain for some time, and be bound as soon as the child wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this swelling from an infected wound or abscess; if it does, cover the wound: if it is treated, as we have said of the splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodulation, and groser than those that come above the foundation, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodulation is old, it works, and shortens moisture above white or subtle blood, and these fistulas never heal; and they are known by the fact that there is egestion or ventosity when the pain makes egestion, and perhaps some verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pass through the bladder, and through half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the hip, and through the back.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the basement, and not passing: and it is that you should prick your index finger or base with a thin needle of silver or iron in the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, if you prick a thin skin of lead or horsehair, as long as you feel the skin or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no perforation egestion or ventosity or ver, as we have said: cut so that it does not pierce more; then hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent near the bladder or near a urinary tract, if it allows urine to pass, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated near the hip joint, then the tendon is close to the bone; if there is no twisting and the location of the pain is not clear, it is because it is stuck, and there is no cure by medicine or ointment; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of those who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and not ancient, in hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the pains are hidden between your hands on its back; and lift the legs up to its knees, and let its knees bent towards its belly; then boil a tent of tin, or lead if there is twisting, until you remove the tent.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the pain is felt around the base, then you should insert your index finger, so that it feels as if it has pierced the bone; and whether you feel between your thumb and forefinger, or the syphilitic sore or the chancre, then cut it out, for there is no need to trouble oneself when it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It can be healed in some cases, but this does not often happen; and the aid that is used is to heat the fine cauterizer according to the width of the fistula, as it has been previously said; and then push it all through the fistula, until it reaches beyond the base; and do this two or three times, until you know that these charred pieces are burnt out, which resemble a barb of an arrow; and then treat the wound with ointment, until those charred pieces are completely gone, then treat the wound with a bandage.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If not, otherwise nothing can be healthy; and if it attempts to enter, and does not perforate just where it is based, and between the attempt and the tent a thick covering of fleece or syfac, and you see the fistula at which the covering points; if the copper begins at the beginning of the fistula, and goes ahead of the tent, and then the cautery after, until it reaches the top of the tent; and he will be delivered from the attempt, and closed; then wash those fleeces that seem like a quill of an eagle, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you cannot remove it, and cut between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization assembles two things: to know, the burning of these charred parts, and the stopping of blood and the separation of moisture; then cure tents made of butter or of choice crushed herbs, until the wound is filled with blood, and the chars are burned in the wound; then cure the wound with hard-boiled onions soaked in durable char, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes from the base, and is away from the body, then press on the neck or foundation, and inquire what.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is the thread or the suture or the charcoal, where it is close to being pierced, then there is no other remedy except hope and faith in one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it from the base, or if you can put tents and cure it as we have said; and do not move too much at first, so that you do not cover the foundation that holds the base, and bring the excretion out through the direction of your will; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and uncover it after it is cut below the foundation, or by tent or other instrument appointed; then clean the char that is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and to stop the fistula in the part before the foundation: if there is a lighter thing to the pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way: and when you push the tent into the fistula, it is found at the cost of the foundation below the skin above, so take a tent perforated at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you push the thread into the fistula, and push the tent along the entire thread into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is not found at the edge of the foundation within, then pull out the thread from that one perforated, so that you push your other or foundation; and take the head of the thread, and assemble the two parts together, and hold them against each other, and leave it there for a day or two; and do not restrain it once, until the thread covers these characters that are between two, and heal; then cure the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then I will pierce it in all ways that you can, unless it is too far advanced.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to try to realign it if it is too far advanced, and then treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinal needle used to make the fistula is very sharp and thin; on the one hand, it is sharp and piercing; and on the other hand, it is not, because we do not know what we should not do, as you see here:
des emorroydes	I do not understand this word in the context of the text
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Body parts can be dislocated in two ways: when they are inside the foundation, like grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some have blood, and some have none, and some are under the foundation and at the bottom of the foundation; but those that are under it have little moisture, and some have a little sharp or a little blood, and they have the color of the body; and the treatment of those who have inside the foundation is that you command the patient to shake his head so he can move into other rooms, as long as the foundations let him go, and it shows the son; if you hurry, and you can hold them with pliers, or you hold them at your angle, then you cut in their roots; and if they cannot hold them for their moisture, take them to a cloth, or a cotton, or a piece of cloth; and you hold them to your two hands, then you cut, and powder over some hot powders that are in the cauterizer; or you cauterize it as it is said in the chapter of cauterization, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the foundations cannot come out, then clean the patient with a biting and rough cloth to wash what is at the foundation, so that it can come out openly; but if the limbs are strong and full of the foundation, then the treatment is light; and it is that you hold them at your angle or with pliers, and you cut, then treat it as we have said, until it is healed, and it does not fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to sew the wound according to this method: take a thread of twisted hair, and make it into a needle, then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread away from the needle, and if it is too wide; and tighten the thread properly, then loosen the thread, and pull out the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to let the excess blood drain; then put above the wound a cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote, and put above the wound, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let him rest until they heal, and when they are healed, treat them with ointment and other treatment until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dryly and firmly on the foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	often occurs in the intestines due to constriction of the body, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to reset the bone at the point of a spatula or your finger's tip, which does not allow it to become moist; then treat it as it should be while it is dry; and if it cannot be treated, start the cut again more strongly than before, until it is fully healed, and then treat it.
dou fremit	dryly
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	formication is a small appearance cut through the skin, and it goes very far; and sometimes the frost finds it, and one feels as if one is dead of formication, and it spreads throughout the body, and more so in the hands than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a needle of a goose feather, or a pen of a vulture very strong, and put that needle on the swelling, until the circle pressed the swelling all around; then turn your hand to all the needle until you cover all around the swelling, and put it in front, and release the swelling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a needle of rain or iron in this form, and be subtle to pull out and draw up:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	and do not pierce, to hold both sides, and press; and if you see, cauterize the swelling, as it is before or chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of this ointment form
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make an ointment with silver or tin, or melted lead or millstones; and never use these small and large tools according to those that they are intended for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those that one should use in the care of children and those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of this ointment, whether small or large, is above broad, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be a difference or the belly is tied as you see, and the belly is pricked inside; and it has on one side two holes, and on the other one; and it should have the belly where one puts the medicines in a beast’s bladder or parchment, and it should be pierced all around with small holes, and there should be between each hole one inch of space, then bolt in these holes one thread of strong thread twisted in ten or around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if the belly is tied with a strong thread, then apply the ointment; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the poultice with oil or vinegar, or something similar, then press it lightly; then squeeze the ministers to both hands together, until it is completely clear, then remove the poultice, and relieve the pain in his legs at the same time, and if the swelling wants to come out, let it come out as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply the poultice in the disease of diarrhea of the belly, and the medicine wants to come out, then start again as long as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if they are stuck at their base, or in an abscess, then the plaster should be as delicate as for a child; and this is the form of the delicate plaster above how the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds:
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to what they are made of, and according to the limbs or wounds that are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by piercing with a spear, and the cut of a sword and a dagger, or of a lance or of a staff or of a arrow, or of similar things; or those that are made according to the limbs of the body, such as a wound that is made above the neck, or above the head, or the eye, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you about the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds to the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	When a simple wound comes to the head or the bone is not broken, take care if it is an embedded arrow or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt lightly of abscess: if you do it immediately cleanse the head itself if there is little blood from the wound, and the cleaning should be on the opposite side of the injured part; and avoid the painful things such as wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to cleanse, then soften his food, and do not drink wine, and do not change his drink; and put on the wound, if abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in sterilized wine; and if there is no abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if his arm has been moved, then put on some ointments, as long as it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword wound and similar, and the lips cannot be closed by stitches, then close them by sewing, as I will say about abdominal wounds, from the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and can be moved, but only held by a small piece, then cover it with a poultice; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat soft foods, such as tests and cooked grain, like chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you have a piece of leather or flesh for a poultice, and it does not reach the bone, then cover the whole wound with it, and pour in warm water, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you have a piece of flesh for a poultice, and it does not reach the bone, then cover the whole wound with it, and pour in warm water, then treat it; and if it does not improve, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the light cure is used: and you should put this powder that boils as soon as the wound has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and the powder finely, and fill the wound, and bind it tightly, until it becomes firm and joins all its parts; then tie it well, and leave it undisturbed, unless it swells; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one should never use chalk alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound has moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, immediately apply this powder; but put on top some ointments digested, or flour of oats made with honey and water, until it heals; then treat other wounds until they are healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then straighten it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about the main fractures afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes from the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and the main fractures, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a bone, there is no other remedy than to let the care, and not put anything restricting, for it hurts bones and makes them withdraw; and do not put anything sharp on the wound, for the substance of the bones is cold, and the continuation of such things is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be gentle, like a sieve washed in hot sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and the bandage washed in hot sweet water, and other stones of this manner, and moist wounds.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then wrap it with bandages until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and the head is shaved and filled with blood, pierce or lower the bone; if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, cover it, and the wound, and cauterize the wound; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the muscle, and the conductor is kept, by which the meat goes, if the cut is above the back of the neck, and do not touch the neck but return it according to its natural shape; then gradually tighten, and leave it for some time, then cure the wounds until they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot, leave them until the wound is closed and healed; and if the wound is fresh, powder over the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then follow the treatment as I have described in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from arrow or sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from arrow or sword, and the wound is deep, look to see if there is any sign of ventosity from the flesh: cut then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh all through with blood, do not put powder in the first hour for the blood so it does not clot prematurely, and return to the heart, and cover the wound; but use attractive ointment, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cloth in the wound to draw out the moisture, and let it rest for three days, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor any trembling of the heart from anything else; and when you see good dispositions, cut that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds of tents and other treatments, until they are healed; and if they cannot be healed, and worked, then make incisions as there is a fistula; thus the cure as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or dagger cut, and it is simple, or small, or at the back, then use the cure for what is in front; if it is large, use stitching; and if it is small, use powder, and if it is embedded in the bone, and has broken pieces, then cover the wound, and remove the foreign bodies if they are not harmful; and if they are not harmful, let the wound rot, it will alleviate the extraction; and for other wounds on other members, use judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	stomach rupture
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the stomach is great and medium and small; from a large wound, the intestines or parts of the intestines may escape once, by which the insertion of them occurs; and the suture is more painful, and often the small wound is worse than the large one, because one can more easily put back the intestines if they are not put back correctly; for the intestines swell quickly when they feel heat, so they are more easily put back if done quickly, and therefore the medium-sized wound is better, because one can more easily return the intestines to their place than other wounds. And there are four ways of stomach rupture: the two common sutures are in the abdominal seam, and the suture of other body wounds and two other sutures are common to other wounds; and therefore they are more suitable with the abdominal seam, and I will explain each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is protruding, and it is easy to replace, it is done in one of the two ways: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen by the heat.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is hot, warm the intestines in this way: moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth with cold water only, or cook it in boiling vinegar and cypress and spike, and roll up the intestine until the swelling is removed; and never do this by force, and it is better to leave it for some time to cool.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is moist with sharp or high and badly cooked foods, because by this the entrance is soon; and if it cannot enter, make a small opening in the instrument with which one copes with worms; and the first cure is to quiet the belly, that we should not cut without great necessity where there is none; and this is the instrument for cutting: if you cut from within the belly and not outside, and pull out the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, if you can put it back in its natural form according to its own place, because this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part away from the belly, it is necessary to place the patient on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part away from the belly, put the head and the worst part higher than the other parts, and thus manage as I said for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wounds are small, you should apply what is appropriate, then put your hands between the ministering remedies that cover the whole wound with their hand, and bring together the lips; this is the common way of stitching, and it is that you hold an needle or several, according to the quantity of the size of the wound, leaving a space of two fingers from the top of the wound, and then thread a needle or good strong thread; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the sinew, which is outside the skin, until you make it pierced from that part, and bring together the two edges of the sinew four times; then tie the thread into a double knot on the needle from two parts, and then bring together the edges of the wound evenly, leaving a space of two fingers, and then thread another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you have done with the needles, until the whole wound is stitched; and let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick, because thin needles cover the whole flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter well: for this reason they should be medium-sized; and do not put the needles too far from the skin and the flesh, so that they do not cover and open the wound before sewing; and then cover the edges of the needles, so that they do not bleed the wound at night, and put tents or cloths on the edges of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is sewn; and this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires one or two needles for the second stitching, and it is that you bring together the edges of the skin and the sinew to a needle with good strong thread; and when you have pierced these edges all four together, then re-thread the needle in the part where you started, in the way one threads a needle; and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of a finger.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was dressed with 15 hours, and it was treated, and it was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mother had thought that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any ointment, for I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicines; and I placed moist cotton twice a day on the wound, and I washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two main ways of stitching: take the needle, and the thread from the part in front of the skin; when it has pierced through the center, then put the tip of the suture or stitch where you have put the needle, and let it pierce on the other side of the part inside the skin; and the understanding of this stitching is that you stitch like the furrier makes furs, and that you leave one end of the suture on one side, and the other on the other, until the stitching is all finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, which Galen properly calls, is such that anyone can do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the main needles to the other head, in a similar way: stick a needle or main needle near, and make it pierce only that part alone, and leave the two heads of the syringe; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the front part just below, the two heads of the syringe; then pierce both from the front part just below, in two other needles that are on the other side; and this is the most common method of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Some say this word, and no one testifies that one should sew the belly with two needles, or have thread in each; and one must put one needle on one side and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and sutures that when the tear is in the belly, it is more painful than other stitches of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you remove the fresh wound from all its blood, if the doctor has moved it, then put back the intestine and the gut; then put powder in the form of chalk, and if the doctor has moved it, then put any ointment that is present, until the wound begins to heal; and bind the bandage, and sound the siphon, and the mirror; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then as soon as it begins to heal, put old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For in other medical conditions with many different wound arrangements where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make communication with principal members, then it is necessary to apply a light bandage soaked in oil of cold or rose oil, and place it around the joints, and remove it from the bones; and if it hurts or feels hot in the belly, and often happens, then you must clysterize with black wine, and immediately if the heat comes to the intestines; and pierce from within, and cut out what is inside, as when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is bare, because of the thinness of its veins that are, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and its approach to the nature of nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the intestine jumps out of the wound, put it back as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned to black, then you must tie the black limb that is there, because there are veins and arteries; then cover what is between the guts, and hang the two ends down from the part outside the wound towards the back to align the extraction when the intestine breaks, and the wound bleeds.
de la routure dou boueil	of the breaking of the boiled
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is punctured, and the wound is small, if one can put it back into a person's belly, because I saw that some men were saved from being gutted by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became a fistula, and inside there was egestion and ventosity; I put care according to what I knew, and did not cease to treat it until it was healed, and the patient recovered.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it being sewn up, I doubted that the hairs were not in his belly; but there was no harm, and he recovered in better conditions, and fed and watered; and some experienced doctors said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, one should be tied in such a way: take firm gauze, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the firm gauze is over the mouth, it holds the mouth above; then cover the wound, and hold it so that it cannot slip off, then put the other firm gauze in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	This chief, if it burns in the intestine, and no harm comes to the hairs, and it can be tied with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the head of this intestine thread that is very dirty, and then tie it to the head of this thin silk thread twisted, then pull the thread into the needle, and through the intestine, and reattach it at the rip; and this method of sewing is no more than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestines, there is no remedy or healing, except for its subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or where she is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	that every wound or abscess, when it is covered, is universally called "fistula", and specifically when it is cut and healed.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.
