And fistula is according to its hard and white root, where no pain is felt, and it is cut and healed like the quill of an eye; and sometimes it is clear and thick; sometimes small and sometimes enough; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no scar, except for one of the eight causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or flesh; or by its malice; or because there is a hard scar inside and on the lips, which does not let new scar grow; or there is too much swelling; or the wound is infected, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late health, and flown by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of fistulas that is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to great veins, and to arteries, and to nerves, or to the face, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if they come to the property of the main member, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this kind are of great difficulty in healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come directly to the bone that I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you know how to treat it, then take a lead or iron tent, if the fistula is straight, if the quarter; and if the fistula is twisted, then take a subtle tent of plaster, because the plasters stick to the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well cover it with tents, then suture one of the holes, for the moisture will not pass from one hole to another, and it cleans; then treat it carefully to your power, that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and it is covered in front, and ask well of the patient about the pain he feels when pressing with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you will know truly the place where it is, and whether it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cover it according to what I have told you, and remove the infected material that is inside; and then treat it as long as it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply embedded in the right place, then cut it open as much as you can, then put soft tents in medicine paste, and press them on the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments of clean healthy charcoal, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cover.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If veins or nerves are not causing you pain or damaging your main limbs, as we have said; and if the tooth is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove the corruption as much as possible until it is completely removed, then treat the things that were injured with charms as long as they are healed; and if they are not healed, and remain the same as before, do not go any further: if it is exposed and you want to remove all the corruption, then remove all the corruption, then restore the tooth; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, it is better to leave it alone, as there is no other way to do it; and if there is a small bone that is corrupted, and you can remove it with pliers, then straighten it with the appropriate tool, and if there are many bones, then remove them all, and do not leave any behind; and if moisture makes it worse, and there is no error or fear, then use moisture and charms to deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, apply a poultice on the wound containing soothing ingredients, and leave it until the flesh is well-covered around the bones, and then they will have more easily broken bones; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, raise the corruption as much as possible until the black part is completely ossified, then cover the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption remaining, and comes close to the bone; if it should be so, cover it all around the corruption, and treat it as long as it is still soft; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The young man was around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the chest, until the matter came to the leg and was inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the doctor by their folly opened it so high that the abscess opened and they poured out many matters, and it became a fistula, and there were many fevers that everyone suffered from sweat and moisture of the body; and many more doctors were called within two years, and there was no cure in the art of hands, until I was called and saw his leg and the medicines they were using to heal it, and what was passing through the fevers caused great pain; and his chest became red and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one was coming into contact with the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	Then I had to remove it, and I cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and I found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming into contact with the bone from within; I saw that the rotten bone appeared to me, and I thought there was no other corruption except what I had seen; and I began to treat the wound with salves for a long time, but I could not heal it; then I re-examined, and discovered the continued corruption in the bone, and I saw it, and then I removed it, and I was unable to heal the limb; but I could only cut around a palm's width of the bone, and I treated it all over its surface, then I applied salves; it became healthy and healed quickly, and it did not need to be re-examined except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurs, but he was healed completely, and in the place of the bone grew a hard callus, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction at all, neither to the other nor to the coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it should be done in this way: take a thin strip of cloth, and extend it at the head of the bone that opens, and command that it be extended upwards; and place another thicker strip of cloth above the first strip, and extend it over the callus that is above the bone, and extend the head, so that you can remove the corrupted part outside, and reveal the callus above the bone where you see it should be, so that it does not rot the callus; and place a bandage or a poultice outside the bone to cover the corrupted part; and it should be done in such a way that one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the tooth is rotted, and cannot be opened, and the decay is in the middle or in one part, then remove the thread from the whole tooth; then sew the decay from one part to another, and let the thread touch the decay only a little, as we have said; and if the decay is in the joint, then cover the joint with the decayed part, and sew the bone or what contains it from the other side; and if the decay is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no other way than to cover it; and if the decay is at the tip of the hand or foot, it is very difficult, but nevertheless you should inquire about that decay, how it opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not let the blood vessel or nerve be damaged; and know that the instruments for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of the teeth, and their size and smallness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason you should prepare an instrument for each kind of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument you have to use, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the instrument you have to use according to what it is suitable for.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints will rot due to causes within or without; and when you have treated the corrosion with medicines, and it does not improve, then you must amputate the member up to the joint where the corrosion comes from, so that the pain escapes by death or by malice, which is greater, due to the lack of the member; and the signs are that the members become black, so that they seem to be burned by fire, and becomes darker afterwards, as the corrosions of the member from member, and take hold of the whole body; if you hurry to amputate, and if the corrosion is at the head of the toe, then cut it off, and do not give it any space for the venom to reach your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes from the hand, if the cloth is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the cloth is at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no other remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and thus do all that the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes to the first joint, if the cloth after the other joint; and if it comes to the bone, if the cloth covers the entire bone; and if it goes up the leg, if the cloth is at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy except that the patient dies; and the way of the cloth or the bandage is such that you tie it above and below, and extend some bands on one side, and some bands on the other side, and moisten the flesh between the two sides to a span wide, until the bone is exposed; then the cloth or bandage, and put a piece of linen on each part so that the bandage does not touch the clean flesh, and it comes to the other injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood comes out when you are working, cauterize the wound strongly, or put some binding powders on it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with a flexible bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in great pain: he had a black swelling that seemed like fire burning, and that corrosion first appeared on his right side, spreading over the whole body; and when the honorable men saw the corrosion, they covered the body, and it was healed; but after a long time, the corrosion appeared again on the right side of the hand, and it came to me, and I put some reflective things on the cleaned body, but I could not stop the corrosions; and he said that I would cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of reflecting the matter; and he also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the virtue of the man was weak; and he lost all hope, and returned to his land, and covered his hand, and it was healed; and I have not told you anything else except for what is done in other cases.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never does an abscess form in a lean limb, and it lingers for so long that it causes great swelling; then it bursts and pierces, and the pus escapes, as if from a vessel; and the skin above is also as thin as cloth, and does not adhere to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such disease is called "sinus", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone from the front, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is that you cover that skin all around, and even when it is thin, as if it were cloth; and it does not heal for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the skin is hardened and decay is not yet complete, and the skin is charred, then use the following ointment: check if the breasts are large, and the nipple is foul-smelling, then use an Egyptian remedy made as follows: take aloe, oil, and frankincense equally, and boil them together in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and thick like honey; then take honey according to your needs, and mix it with water and make an ointment of the breasts, and apply it to the wound and tightly bandage it; leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by sprinkling; do this many times until the breasts are clean and free of pain; if the pain cannot be borne, and the Egyptian remedy or the ash water does not work, then use an ointment made of honey and wine with a little frankincense broken up; or use an ointment made of honey and melted honey that has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine makes the flesh sore; when you have done this, and you are sure the breasts are clean, then use an ointment made of char and oil and rose water, and make it with a little frankincense; if the nipple is too small, and the ointment cannot enter, then enlarge it with a needle and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is large enough; if the wound is too large, then leave it alone so that the skin or the ointment can enter, and if the nipple that is above the ointment is sore, then cover it with a cloth or lower bandage where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement. Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts are not well digested after many hours, it is necessary to press them so that they do not harden.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the pouch of the hand, or from the palm, or by chance in other places; and when it is opened, and no care is taken, if the abscess extends to the root of the finger, and possibly entirely, and comes to corrosions just to the bone, as long as there is pain, and the affected area is large and red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, then you must remove all the excess that remains from the finger, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is healthy and the joint is sound; and if the joint approaches the skin quickly, and begins to prick, and the wound, then it is necessary that you put the cautery away from the joint so that it does not pierce, and bring the end upwards, and cover this char subtly and gently, and put above the remaining part of the char hot and corrosive medicines to remove all; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cover it and drain, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be healed; and if you see the other also corrupted, then cover it with a subtle and gentle cloth as before said, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is fierce, and bleeding, and it feels great pain, then it is necessary that you first heal it; then cover the joint with a subtle and gentle cloth cut across, and make sure that the cut does not reach the part of the char that is outside the joint, for the hairs would feel too much pain; and if there is, then put something on top to relieve.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the hand should be soft
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Those who are born in the hands of some men by chance are all charred, and sometimes they have bones, and sometimes they have a hook, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in any of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born in no finger of the hand do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the hand, sometimes move; the size of the charred one is light, in this way: cut it at its root into a wide spatula.

For those who are born or must have at the back not, it is necessary that you first cut the round flesh to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable silk for this, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same things that come together in this way come either by birth or by wounding or by burning of fire or by similar things.

des vils	of the wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Vis are veins large and swollen full of superfluous melancholy, which come from many members of the body; and more so in the legs of those who stand and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you give it once purgation of black bile, and then the healthy from the basilisk.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is done in two ways: one is that you apply it and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you open the vein and let it all flow out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The tailor is done in this way: first, the leg of a high, very hot iron, so that the large one is not subtly heated, then straighten the leg with the bad pain below the hip; then cut the vein in I, II or III, with a wide gash, then release and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one to the other, until as much blood as the bad pain can bear is drawn; then tie it off, and command him to be shaved of meats boiled with black coal; and start the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are flat, and not swollen with the bad pain.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. The fire cauterization method is as follows: if the leg has long and even hairs, first shave them, then place it in hot water or steam until it turns red and swells the veins; if you don't have hot water, heat it over a fire, and apply a warm poultice to the affected area, either on the thigh or below the knee; then apply the flesh side of raw meat to the wound, and scrape off any discoloration from every part until it appears as if you were scraping a white cord; then remove the raw meat, and bandage it lightly with linen; then apply a cool poultice for about three days; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it to the wound, as you have done before; then apply another bandage, as many times as necessary; then cut away the discolored skin and lift it, and apply a new bandage to the second wound; then strip away the bandage from one layer to another, until it is all clean; then apply another bandage; and if you cannot pull and lift it, insert an needle through the thread very tightly, and pull and lift it, and remove the thread, turning your hand from one side to the other until it is all out; be careful not to let it stick, for if it sticks, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it causes harm to the wound; then place a soft cloth soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the eye is contracted and twisted and swollen together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must torture it severely but do not cover it; and treat it as we have previously described.

de la voinne civile	of the vein civil
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is inserted in the legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in land where there is no moisture; and by chance it arises from another part than the legs, and if there is a pus that comes out of the skin, as it comes from within the flesh and muscles, insert between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are such that a very large inflammation comes in the leg, then the limb changes, and the wound begins to protrude, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the wound is open, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of cloth about one and a half inches wide and long enough to cover the leg, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it is not needed, if it is wrapped around the cloth, and covered with a bandage; if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remaining part, and do not cover its root until it is completely out; because if you cover it, it will go back into the wound, and cause abscess and putrefaction of the limb, and severe illness; therefore it is necessary that it be treated little by little from the top, and nothing remains or rots; and this wound never occurs when it is treated with the palm of your hand, or ten fingers long, and some have come to me, because it was ten fingers long, and when you cover it, if it swells or bursts, and pierce it from the bottom, so that everything comes out; and remove the matter inside, and administer medicines in a salve for putrefaction every day, then cure it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And often times at this vein, and especially when it opens in the joint of the little finger, or the big toe, and much pain comes, and it suddenly falls back; therefore as we have said before, you must do as follows.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	verses that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cow disease", because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and goes up and down the body, and is felt by each member to member, until it burrows into the skin where it went, and jumps out; and it is caused by some humors, such as worms and leeches and tapeworms or intestinal worms; and people doubt its harm, because as it goes through the body, and goes up to the head, and comes to the oil, perhaps it enters, and destroys the oil; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see that the patient is curable and can be treated, then it is necessary to place the limb above and away from a very tightly bound joint, then cut across and remove it, and if the blood comes out in front of the char, you do not remove it, but cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrodes the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or approaching near the oil, then hold it away from it firmly, then cut across and remove it; and it is necessary to use the remedy of healing of the bodies of medicines dissolved for the bad humors for the diseases.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen what I will tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered one of her arms, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it rise like a worm in the shoulder, faster than anything, as if it were live silver when it cuts through flesh; the pain departed from that arm, and moved to the shoulder, and then a little later corrupted all over her body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that she had turned inside out around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from one member to another, for I had never seen this disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Indeed, I had seen that it could move from one limb to another, but I had not seen it in this way before; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry skin, and her veins were exposed, and because that vulnerability appeared constrained; and it did not happen in the same way to those who are delicate, and who have moist skins and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see how to cure this disease, and the pain feels as we have said, if it appears as we have mentioned, then firmly hold the limb above and below, and then apply a caustic to the skin; and if you do not see it at your eyes, then treat the vulnerability as we have said, with fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their similarities and according to the types of bodies they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of them is such that there are those with large points, and small, and barbed, and soldered; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one which pierces any member according to the manner: whether in a principal limb it pierces as in the neck, head, heart, lungs, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it pierces therefore in any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you next, appears: then it is necessary that you attempt the extraction of this arrow, for the death comes after in many ways; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not completely out, then pull it, and care for the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the head when the arrow pierces and perforates the bone, and the spasms that occur above the brain, are blindness and dizziness and vomiting and swelling of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without strength in the nose or in the ears; and perhaps without speech and voice; and a white discharge from the wound that resembles pus, and also like boiling oil; and if these signs appear to you, then keep the arrow if it has not been removed.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of a shoulder dislocation when it occurs or breaks, are that it is near the right breast, and feels as if it was stuck in a hard thing, not empty; and perhaps the shoulder also moves like a chicken, and in cutting out black blood, and comes with coldness and cold sweat, and syncope: therefore, without doubt, the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a wound that does not promote healing is that without any foam coming out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the limb changes color, and it breathes high and seeks the heat.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead pierces into the covering of the lower back, it is behind the small ribs; and it causes great pain and shortness of breath, and moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead pierces into the stomach, by chance if it jumps out of the wound, nothing of the undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead pierces into the belly, and does not jump out through the intestine rupture, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead pierces into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes out afterwards, and the pain is very great: it is certain that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and back and spine and hip and knee and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a limb or an artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow in his arm at the root of the nose: I tried to remove it, and took it out from the other side of the ear grease, and was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in a horse, an arrow was stuck that went through the grease of the oil paper, and the arrow was removed, and it could only reach to the point facing the fist, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, all of iron without ears; the horse was healed, and no bad accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And an arrow was taken from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I cut off the barbs, and carefully removed it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And an arrow was taken from a man, which was in his neck or belly, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	If you wish to treat a person who has an arrow stuck in their back or chest, and the wound was closed over; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural positions, and found no harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to treat another person who had an arrow stuck in their face, and the wound was closed over; and it remained thus to suffer great pain; and many others similarly.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And if you wish to treat an arrow to the man of the king, who had it in his neck, and was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely healed, I was called to cure after it had been three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I carefully opened it with a very thin needle, and I did not feel anything; and he felt no pricking or pain outside his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow that I put on his forehead with a strong adhesive bandage, because the wounds did not inflame; and I saw the arrows on his forehead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I then applied the bandage again, and immediately healed the wound, and the pain lasted a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied medicinal acid to the wound with my hands, as long as it was open, and tested it, and felt the tip of the arrow that was embedded in the flesh; then I inserted more medicinal acid into the wound opening, until the arrowhead appeared visibly; and it passed well through the four months, and then rotted if the wound that I had sown with needles, and on one side and the other, and could not get out; therefore, I did not cease to subtilize and engineer in various ways of instruments, until I got good needles, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I sown it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the miracle worker judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it then, and it was sewn up, and the pain was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you might place your care where I did not say, for books cannot comprehend everything; but wise masters know well many things, and know what is present and deficient, thus finding new work, and new instruments, in the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of the limbs or they are removed because of two ways: either by the way they enter, or from another part; and the one that goes out through the way it enters, is an arrow entered into its flesh, and it never came out.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her remain until the charcoal is completely burned out, and the issue is alleviated; and also if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot escape, let her remain thus for several days, and move her every day; and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, pierce around all the forest subtly, until the bones around are expanded, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the head bone, and goes towards one of the belly's ventricles, and any of the accidents that I have previously mentioned causes pain to the patient: do not draw it out immediately, but let her remain thus for several days, because if the arrow comes towards the face, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck in the bone only, and does not come out on its own, and remains there for several days without causing harm, then use the method to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply stuck and cannot be pulled out, then apply tar around it as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the tent; and if you feel it, then remove it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bone, nerve, or vein, then wait until the wound is large enough to remove it; and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has ears attached that hold it in place, then cut the flesh that is stuck to it with a sharp knife, and then break or pry open the ears of the arrow, until you can remove it; and be careful not to break the arrow while removing it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do it once, then place the lain around the shoulder until it is properly positioned, then pull it out, because the extraction is alleviating.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding from the vein goes against you, follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and guard against incising the nerve and the vein, and put in place as you can draw out the arrow without danger, or soon or late, firmly or roughly; and put the pain according to the form it was in when the arrow fell off, for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then follow what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens nothing of it, or the skin is inflamed in a place where we can see or feel it: cut then above, as much as the hooks can take, and then extract it: if it suddenly breaks now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, round your hand and push it into the bone, until it enters the bone, and expands the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if there is any of the arrow left, and you have to administer it little by little, if you are administering the instrument with a hook, so that the point of the arrow enters the hook; and then pull out, and if the arrow is hooked, pull the instrument in, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut out all of the flesh around where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is stuck in the neck or back or stomach or bladder or ribs, and it is close to them, and you can cut over it, if possible; and do not cut into the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then treat the wound if necessary; and the cure until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the needles used to extract arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and this is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the beak of a bird, to put at the point of the arrow, such as this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the barbs for inserting and removing is such as this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins common to the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins that can be tapped from, of which there are sixteen heads, namely: two veins that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the temples apparent; and the two veins that are in the arm pits of the eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two jugulars that are on the neck; and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the six veins that are outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly opened are five in each arm: the one is to the cephalic, and is on the right side, and is called by the people "the main vein of the head"; and the middle is called "the forearm", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and is called by the people "the vein of the chest"; and the basilic is on the left side, and is called by the people "the vein of the belly", and is above the foscile, and is that which is opened, which opens manifestly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the auricular and the anular, and it is on the right arm; and in the leg and where the knee is, there are three veins: the one is outside the corbeure of the pouch of the right side costeit, and the second which is at the knee of the left costeit; and the vein which is called "nesse", which is at the knee of the other costei; and in the other leg are three veins.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The treatment of veins after the ears helps with old catarrhs and headaches; and the qualities of the treatment, as I told you, is to remove the main cause of the pain, and to rub the skin where the veins are on a rough cloth; then squeeze the veins at their base with a cloth until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places: then apply your finger there, and where you feel the hair coming out of your finger, cut it; then take the lancet and poke it just outside the vein next to the bone, then lift your hand up the whole vein, and scrape and the skin and the vein should be crossed over well, and let the blood come out until you see it; then strain and tie, as long as it is clean; and I have already mentioned the incision and the cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The translation of the first sentence is: "For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The purging of the vein in the front is as valuable as the purging of the cerebral diseases and facial old diseases, and headaches, and rheumatism; and the quality is such that the pains are strange, twisting their neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called «fosseur», which has the following form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point above the vein, and hold it with your hand or another thing, and let the blood issue according to the quantity you see; then loosen the neck of the patient, and tie the vein until it is healed and never again in a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Therefore, it is not necessary that the flame be too hot; and the position of the bone is important, because the bone is close, and by chance it may break the flame when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The position of the second veins that are in the two armpits helps with the elbows, and the wrist, and the palm, and the back of the hand in the oil, and for diseases of the face; and the quality of their position is such that the pain is strange when twisting any limb, as before; then the position, and let the position be on the other side, a little bit long of the flame, a little bit wide, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, perhaps they will break; then correct the blood, as much as you have skill, and then tie with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bloodletting of the vein is good for ague, and for fevers, and for facial diseases such as migraine and headache that come in the face, and constantly when it is old; and the quality of the bloodletting is such that the pain is strained on its neck, then strain its vein to your right hand, and take the thin flame long, and put it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well, and the blood will start to flow; and do not move too much in front, and correct the blood according to your need, then tie it for a night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the second compound helps to narrow the alainne, and at the beginning of the ulceration, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corrosions, and in herpes, and in estomenes; and the quality of the salve is such that the pains strangely separate from each other, as we have said; and so the masters are above the chief of the pains, and the pains lie on one side, then cleanse the wound with a long, slightly wide blade, then drain the blood constantly, or as much as the matter requires; then do the other side in the same way, then remove the bandage, and hold both wounds evenly, that the pains do not entangle; and let it rest until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the lips above helps to cure in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cuts of the lips, and sores inside and out.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to make the pain sit in front of you, and hold its neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: cover both of them, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt, cover the largest of each part, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the tongue's disorder
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The disorder of the veins that are outside the tongue helps after the disorder of the cephalic, and it is the narrowness of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the sailor is that the maladies cease between your hands before the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks at each side a black vein: therefore healthy one and the other, and do not move too much in front, because outside are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.
