The veins of the jaw that are commonly cured are cured in two ways: either by pinching all the flame wide, or with a thin slice as if cutting through, and is called "aneurysm"; and they are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very famous, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has skill to open veins that are closed and have thick blood and turbid; and this is the form of the flame mirror.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more delicate, and is for cleaning fine veins, where there is fine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and under the collarbone, and in the arm, and in the stomach; and it is important for the cleaner to clean carefully, and to withdraw the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if the artery is cut, and blood flows, it should be cooled, as I have said; and it should not be touched with the flame, but cut as with scissors.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, it should be stretched and changed, or you may see any sign of blood in it, or you may open the vein in place of the arm: it opens clearly; and it should be coped with scissors as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know the vein of the sinew, it should also be stretched, and you touch the vein until you feel the pulse; then sign the vein with a needle, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with scissors; and watch that you do not cut into the artery when you see the vein swell, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a stream flowing out as high as the urine of a child, and the stain is red and thin, it is from the artery: hurry then, and place your finger longwise, then remove your finger without stopping, as it often does; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the painful parts; and be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the stain is not stopped, and it hurts, and the medicine is not present, if the artery opens, for the blood flows out; stop the stain.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a small splinter of the thistle, and make it into a poultice, and place one half on one side and the other on the other side; if there is no pain, it is good; if there is pain, as we have said, use the ointments that relieve pain; and the reliefs are not greasy in many positions for the small wound of the sore, and the position of the joint of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The salve of the vein in the middle helps to treat blood that is above and below, because it is composed of basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the salve to be applied to all the nerves that are out of place, and if it does not too much in front, and he finds the nerve, and he swells and the ointment is either greasy, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often opens, and if it does not open in any man by its subtlety, then you should use the salve from the instrument anesil; and protect the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein is helpful, as it draws blood from the head, and helps with it; and it is best to prick in the olive or oleander fire, for it is the safest of all veins, as it has no connection with nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is best to seek the lightest vein, and do not hurt anything if you cannot find it the first time, and start again; and perhaps some men's veins swell at first, but it does not hurt.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about health is that health is not maintained except to maintain health and to prevent diseases from coming; and let health be done in one of the three veins that are or cost: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilic; and if it should be done at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after fasting, when the sign of repletion appears; and if it should be done on the first day or the third, after two hours or three in the morning.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The remedy that is administered to diseases does not have a determined time, but rather when needed, at all hours and in all situations; and it does not matter to suckle children under 14 years, nor to give medicine to pregnant women except for labor pains from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should one administer remedies to the elderly who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wants to administer remedies, in any way whatsoever, it is necessary that they first clean the intestines from a light clyster, if they have too much retained feces, so that the veins do not absorb excessive and harmful substances into the main members; and one should not administer remedies to those who are too fat from meats, or drunkards, as much as they may be, nor hydropiques; and if one wants to administer remedies after colic passion, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent travel, pregnancy, watching, and fasting, and all the virtue, whether by arm or body; then subtly the humors, if they are not too heavy, by foods and drinks and medicines, if one has them; then take a bath or abstain from anything that does not prevent, to subtilize the blood, and cure the vein around the third hour, as we have said; and guard against work, needle, luxury, and similar things; and be tied and joined, and let the remedy be higher than that of whom one administers, and let the arm rubbed twice or three times, then gently move the joint above the middle, because when it is too stiff or weak, it cannot correct itself; then rub the remedy on the hand until the veins swell, and feel the pain; then mollify the remedy with a drop of old oil, then put its due amount on the right hand over the vein of the hand where one wants to administer, that the vein does not fail to strike.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that flee as quickly as strings to the sieve, and there are some that are plain in their softness, such that when one puts them over the flame, they withdraw from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus are those; and if it opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, because it is necessary that the sieve be careful in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, then one should try again a little below that place or above, if the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflamed, and the pain spreads, one should leave it alone or rest for a day or two, and not tie the arm: perhaps an abscess will form; do not enter or take a bath, then try again with the sieve if it suits him; and if the wound is small, or if one cuts subtly and doubts that there is as much blood as one saw, then put the fire directly on that wound; and work a little hastily, as long as the veins are inflamed; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb swells, do not restart the wound, and put a small amount of oil on it, because it alleviates the course of the blood, and it is good for this limb that the oil; and thus administer the oil in every wound that you heal the wounds, to stop the course of the blood; and the same thing does triangular and bow-shaped, when put on the limb; if subtly the blood and sparks when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes large abscesses that often occur, exactly when it is not healed except at this time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the limb soft sponge in hot and in a cloth a little wet, and hold it an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of the blood from the vein, and if it remains in the limb for any time no longer or greenish, then do not put anything on it; and if you see, put on any thing of aloes or of myrrh mixed with honey, mustard or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and appearance of the saint's head at the basilica: place your hand on it, and if you press the bone too much with your hand, that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not place anything that we have said on it, for inadvertently you may cut the artery; but apply a dry poultice to harden the bone, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the amount of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it turns red; and if you see that it is thick, let it bleed until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for one who is in pain and out of place, and has the task of extracting arrows, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for the weak, do the opposite, and let them rest often, and it should be bandaged by cutting across, not by pinching; and this method of bandaging is safe from the separation of arrows and the entanglement of nerves, and it is better than the bandaging done long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one who has a weak body for the bandaging, it is fitting to give bread made from ground apples; if they are heated, take out the arrow three times or four times; and if they are of cold constitution, change the bread made from ground apples before the bandaging with mustard bread, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and strongly scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he palms the pain after much bleeding, it is necessary that he drink broth of bone, and sweet-smelling syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to stretch an arm, and bleed again, it is necessary that, when he is weakened by much bleeding, he should bleed a little and a little, according to the amount of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to bleed an arm after the first bleeding, and he has great strength, he should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal from the other side, should heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated, and causes fever; if you need to draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein until it bleeds well; then you must restore all the conditions of healing, and place your hand on top of the wound when it is healed, so that the dead does not return in place of the wound, and this has happened many times, when the healer is negligent; and it does not matter if you see the arm bleeding, and draw out blood the second time, and the vein is closed, that you press firmly on top; or if it is curved, that you extend the arm quickly, for this would be bad; but let it heal the second time; or until the unhealthy part is removed from the vein, and put a small amount of fresh salve on the wound, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the swelling is present, let it be and do not press it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood the second time, if the healthy vein in the same limb or in another vein or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthy in place of the main vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of drawing blood is that the vein bursts with sharp heat, until the blood is red; then it is gently moved, so that the vein appears well, then draw blood across, not too narrow or too long; and let the punctures be wide, and draw blood well near the joint of the hand, and if none can come out, if you put the hand in sharp heat, and let the blood flow in the sharp, until you have enough; and if it is still not coming out, do not repeatedly put the hand in sharp heat, for it will be worse than before; and drawing blood from this vein is safer than all other veins, there are no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve of the hand of the right side is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how: strain the hand, and boil in very hot water until the vein is out, if one sees it; and if the salve goes against, and if you cover it with everything, it will not hurt anything; and do not move it too much, for the nerves are all nude of char, and then put the hand in very hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as necessary, put oil and thread on the wound to sew quickly, and thus do for each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve for the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the sage is good for all diseases that are outside the body, such as marsh diseases, retention of urine, and kidney diseases, and old leg and arm diseases, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its salve is that diseases are quickly dispersed in hot, piquant water, and rubbed on the vein until it perishes, and binds over the joint of the pain; and the vein is at the elbow, and through the pain, many rains go out; therefore the salve is good for large veins, or at the elbow, that moves.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you find the healthy ones above the skin, and they are removed from the dead, and the healthy one crosses as in sewing; and let the flames burn.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be removed without any, reset the skin in the hot, and let the blood drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if it is necessary to first clean the healthy one, then start the second above a little, for the first is salted; do not doubt the tendon, as we have said, and so make the other side of the skin equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The first blood from the vein is at the elbow, and its cleaning is worth the pain of the back, when it is for an arrow.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its health is such that the hairs between or bathing, and it is strange above the ankle four times in twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways you can, and in various directions; and it is better to cover it, because the feet are clean, and it is very easily infected by handsmen.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not treat it, it will heal none of the blood that opens or drops from the wound, and towards the little toe, and it guards against the nerves; and correct so much blood as you see, and then remove the ligament, and put it on cotton and hold it in place; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or of tin, or of glass; and ventosation is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without pricking is done in two ways: either all fire, or without fire; and suction done by pricking and drawing blood is done in twelve places on the body, of which one is all over the chest; and the others are under the collarbone; and the other two are on the ribs; and the suction below the chin; and the suction on the shoulders; and the suction on the hips; and the suction on the arms; and the suction on the legs; and the suction on the ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the body, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone, as one does when drawing blood; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease caused by repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessity of diseases requires ventilation, or for customs, then we should stir up each hour at the beginning or end of the month, or in every ten; for there are some who, when they have need of ventilation, have heavy breathing; and there are some who experience repletion and tightness in their face, and in their head, and in their throat; and there are some who taste blood in their mouth, and extend their tongue, and suck blood; and there are some who sing, and see through a mist of blood and nausea and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the month of May, we command them to fast for three hours after midday.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The fasting of the mouth helps to cure the headache … that comes from them, and should only be done after the evacuation of all the blood; and this fasting is in place of the fasting of the cephalic, and should not be used by those who are of cold complexion or who have diarrhea, for this does great harm; and therefore it is not suitable for those who are awake or who have other cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often feel better, if they become forgetful, and for this reason, you should put the bandage a little lower due to the uncertainty of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The bandage around the neck is in the place of the head and the temple, and for this reason, it is best to place it at the narrowest point, and at the base of the jugular vein, and all over, and at repletion; and it should not be placed too tightly, as it may cause forgetfulness or stomach ache or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The bandage on the two sides of the neck is good for headache, and obtundedness and emaciation, and choking, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the healing of the temple; and you should command the patient to put his hand when placing it, that he does not press the artery, and does not cause bleeding of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The breathing through the nose is beneficial for diseases of the mouth, and for corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the health of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The breathing through the shoulders is beneficial for diseases that come from heat and filling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The breathing through the elbows is as beneficial as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and commands the healthy one not to be too eager in the beginning, for the arms are bare of clothing, and can cause veins and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is placed on the back should be used for hernias, and to remove dislocations, and it should be large and made of metal, so it can properly pull; and if it is too thin, it may break; and I cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg suction cups should be used widely, as they draw blood from the entire body, and are useful for old pains of the rain, and the marsh, and the bladder, and they remove clots; and they are in place of the two thighs, and everywhere they weaken the body after long use, and cause pain in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method for applying the vacuum is that you first apply it empty and quickly succeed, then press it strongly and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the limb red and swollen, and appear the outflow of blood; then stop, and replace the cups, and take care in the position of the body, for there are those who have thin skin and clear flesh: it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and one deeply; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the skin is thick, then it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thinly pierce the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very severe, then you must prick the third time; and when we want to draw out the arrow little by little, we should only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to draw out much blood, we should often recommend it; and if the wound is not severe, then prick it in front, and the end should be that the keel is pierced deeply, and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and are strong, and who have sharp teeth, that you apply the leeches of oil that is appetizing and dissolving: if it is in this state, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, of pennyroyal oil, or of lily, or of camomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of tarr, or balm, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is to be sewn has wide and large pores, then it is not necessary to put oil, but it should be washed after the application of sharp vinegar, or cold vinegar, or vinegar of myrtle, or vinegar of cucumber, or vinegar of porcelain, or another similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ash, or sharp vinegar, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive superfluities rise from old wine, or from vinegar of sucking, or from decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and they should not be immediately washed with a suction device before the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and they should not sleep immediately after the suction, and it is recommended that they move around, when they should be sucked and when they are being sucked.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are sick are choleric, and if they have too much bile and are inflamed; it is recommended that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and leeks at the table, and similar things; and pulp of pears, and char of Chartres, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold constitution should take honey syrup, aromatic wine between old and new, and a little vinegar, pomegranate juice, and small olives and pigeons; and on the day they are to be ventured, they should drink more than usual; and it is recommended to give some myrrh or musk to some men before or after the venture to strengthen the main members; and the wine should not be subtle, but only those who are hot should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed on the body are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and the gallbladder, and on the stomach and the belly and the kidneys and the buttocks, because these members do not suffer from pressure except to draw blood from one member to another, as we put suction cups on the breasts when the baby is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the stomach and on the belly to soothe the member; and to remove pain, when there is an abscess or a stone, by its attractive power it may happen to remove the abscess or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it is done when placing it on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty for drainage alone; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes with a hot bath of sharp herbs, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot sharp herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the pneumatic device administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two inches of width and half a palm of length, and has or costates around the middle one small hole, as to put an needle, and it is of tin, sulfur before so that it does not burn the skin when putting it on the limb; and it has in the middle a crossbar of tin or iron, for putting a candle, and they are large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the suction devices of children are different from the old, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this suction cup in such a way on the limb: take the candle of wax or the liniment, and put it inside the suction cup through the rod that is inside the suction cup, so that the light may be at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the hairs; then place it on the limb, and do so as we have said, so that when one wants, if the vapor rises, and remove the suction cup; and take the liniment as before, and repeat often, if you have the opportunity.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup that is used in the disease of pleurisy, at all times, there is no rod or stopper, and it is not administered until it is full of air, and it is placed on the limb entirely alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Sansues are not treated except in members where one cannot place suction for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in similar members, remove the char, such as two or teeth, and others similar; and the quality of the user is such that when you trueve sansues that are in sweet waters without pressure, take them; and put them in sweet water until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then cleanse with blood and suction, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the sansues; and when they are plain, and cherrched, if it is a member where one can place suction, place it, because this is very helpful afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, raise the limb gradually and well, and then wipe it; if the wound is too large after the furrows of the sinews, then moisten a piece of linen in cold water, and place it on top, until the wound is cleansed; and if the wound multiplies, then place on top vitriol broken into pieces, or salves, and similar things, until it is cleansed; or you place half-peeled beans on the limb, and leave them until they burn the limb, to stop bleeding now; and if you have more need, take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the snakes do not want to take, rub the wound with fresh blood, or you insert a needle so that the snake bites it, and then place them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will die; and when you see that they are dying, powder with a little aloe and beaten silk, or ash, so they will now burn.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	So, dear child, that the foolish might see this chapter, they have never seen any of the old books, nor have they read any letters; and for this reason, the science is hidden in our land, for I found none good; and I know nothing, except by the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated it, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that will be needed, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and stay on the truth, so that those who are experienced find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or bruising comes to any part of the body, it is necessary that you hasten to treat the injury on both sides, if nothing happens, such as weakness of the body, children, or old people; or if the pain is not very great, or too sharp; and use cold remedies, that is to say, cold compresses, and chicken broth, and do not drink wine, and do not use any heavy meats, and do not fill up too much with food that fills the veins of blood, until you have no doubt of abscess or spreading of matter to the member; if the pain returns as it has used to.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to apply a thick poultice of meat that makes large blisters, or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat, and rice, and tests, and peas, and chicken breasts, and eggs, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the poultice should be changed often and more quickly than the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the elderly and infirm do not mend well or heal according to their nature due to the weakness of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but rather, reset the broken bone over the joint and join the member together, as it was before; and do not let it rest entirely, and for this reason, it is necessary to apply a thick poultice of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And there are many ways in which bones can be broken.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the shoulder is different from the fracture of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes through, and another when wetting, like the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture at one small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each way has its own method, and its proper instrument in restoration, according to what memory comes in the limb; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted, and open well by itself, and it is to be pressed with the hand; and when there is no twistiness or touching, and the pain is not much, if there is no fracture; but it can have twistiness, or cut, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It does not matter if you move it with your hand, but put the remedies that come after this, and then gently constrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And if the fracture that was in the arm, and the two parts are disjointed, you should now put them evenly, as much as an abscess comes; and if an abscess is hard and comes, do not leave any joint, until the abscess is calmed; then put it even to the muscle that you can lightly and safely, and if the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of those who have pieces; then constrain, as it should be after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces, if it is in the hand or foot, or at your hand if it is small members, or to two strings, or to a string and at your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the member broken are separated, if you can join them together as best as you can, and guard that by your work no harmful injury or pain comes; and well set the two broken bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well in your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if it feels beautifully, and do not strain it too much, and do not press it as those who bring it by their work aposteme and contraction of the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is set, properly restrain the painful part so it does not move, whether awake or sleeping, turning or in any other way; and ensure that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not yet set properly, and it should be placed in the correct position so that it feels no pain; and guard that it is put straight, for twisting will not come when it is restored; and the quality of the member broken is as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The members broken are different in size, greatness, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as the arm and leg, and similar ones: if they are thin, cover them with fine linen cloths; and those that are thick, such as the thigh and calf: if they are large, cover them with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bands embrace the whole member evenly, and hold it equally from all parts, so that there is no gap; then wrap lightly around three or four times according to the length of the member, and hold your hand a little on every part of the bandage, then go above the break and hold it less, than the break slowly remove a little from the break; then soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another bandage and turn around again on the broken member; then return to the part away from the break, and hold it gently, neither too hard nor too painfully, as we have said in the first chapter above; then put between the bandages linen or cloth, as much as they are equal, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made fingers on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, put something soothing on the abscess, and what removes the inflammation, and let it be like this for some time; then place it on the wounds, and be of half a wide bandage, well-sewn, or of wood from which the splints are made, or of palm leaves, and they should be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the splint that one puts on the fracture should be a little larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as it is needed for the limb of small or large size; then place the splints as you have done in the first chapter, then tie them together with a thread evenly, as you did in the first chapter on the fracture; the tighter it is, the less; and it should be that the threads are medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be of flax; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of the folk who make the cords of linen thread, and this is great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should only have between each splint about two fingers' space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are closed by the strings of the needles after the straining in their clean state, then put them out of the cloth or other clean rag so that it does not become infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splint, and the bandages are broken, I will tell you the treatment here afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And it is not necessary to strain all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put on bandages until after five or seven days, or more depending on your safety from abscess: and see the method of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take some flour that is held as in the walls of the mill, and mix with an abundance of egg, and put this mixture, not too clear or too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring fracture to many positions, and especially to women and small children, because it is not too hard or too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to treat fractures and dislocations and twists: take equal parts of aloe leaves, mugwort, Arabic gum, and myrrh, each X amount; myrrh and aloes, V amount; achillea, VIII amount; and make a powder, and mix with honey; if the body's condition is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and it heals broken bones quickly, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster that is good for twists: take mugwort and valerian, each X amount; myrrh and aloes, VIII amount; acacia, VI amount; Armenian bole, X amount, and grind well, and mix with vinegar or honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to treat joints and bones that are diseased from their sockets, and to relieve the pain coming from them, and to use the bone, and the breaker: take a new one, and moisten it in oil and heated oil, and put on top of the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not last long, but they are good for relieving abscesses and properly treating pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat broken bones that lasts: take dried fig leaves and earthworm castings, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of treating the fracture of a bone and to lessen the pain of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of almonds, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with fresh coriander juice, or dried, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of treating more than the first, when an abscess is coming to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of wormwood, and seeds of linseed, balm, melilot, and sanicle, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part; and grind, and mix with salt juice, or sweet juice, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb except for a cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to restore it, things that are dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat wounds and pain: take mallows and horsehair, or feathers of an owl, and egg whites, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a poultice and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, after a little while, take care not to feel any pain, nor if the bones of its limb are dislocated; if not, do not release it by hand again. And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, without rest or inflammation, quickly release it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light bandage, and moisten with sea water, and rinse in hot water, and lift the limb until the itching stops, and soothe the pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in hot or rose oil, and tie up with a nut, as long as you are sure of no abscess forming; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and soothe the pain, then restart the subtle binding, and a little plaster, and do not strain it too hard as before; subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is filled with pus and redness and pain and swelling, and you have skill in applying ointments and poultices, then restart as you did before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb at all as we have said, then do not delay for three or four or five or seven days; and never leave it more than twenty days, according to what we see, until the fracture is set, and approaches the joint of the bone above; then it holds more than before, and increases its strength, as I have said before; and if you see that the limb is setting more than is necessary, then cut away the callus that cannot come again; then apply hot water often when you reset it, and this every hour, and loosen a little the bandage; by this method, then the callus is removed from the limb, and quickly repair what the foolish doctors do, which tortures the member: this is bad, and if it is not done properly, I see nothing else but weakness and doing it straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various breaking methods
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many breaking methods are, and various figures, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks that are made by the impact of a spear, and the collarbone fractures the entire bone just under the shoulder blade, which is outside the bone, as it does in the neck or the back; and because of this method of breakage is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear pierces the bone from above in a transverse direction, and this method of breakage is called "absolute"; and it is the wound of these two breaks large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact with a blow, or a cut from the spear, or a fall on the stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is a broken bone that approaches the skin near the bone, or on top of the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is set in the bone as thinly as a hair, and the fracture is small, and because of this it is called "hair-like" fracture; and if the wound made by a spear, or by falling, or by something similar, and allows the piece of bone to enter below, and the threads are like those used by hatters when they set them on the hats; then the spear enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are those who have or suffer from moist bones, such as children; and they have all these kinds of fractures where small pieces are dislodged like these; and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the removal above them, and the examination with tents, and by the corrupted flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known because when one has revealed the bone, and one rubs it above, if there is an open fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of accidents from evil, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of consciousness, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes issuing forth and reddening, and other similar things in many conditions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any obvious injury, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fractured bone comes first to you, and it is in the leg, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day, so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the arm, then you should remove the bone before the seventh day, as long as the flesh around the bone is not decayed, and the injuries that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fractured bone comes close to the tissue that covers the brain, then it is necessary to cut away the part that is injured in this way: and you should grab the head of the painful wound, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound as softly as you can, and if blood comes out when exposing the bone, or an abscess forms, help with what is necessary, and it is necessary to fill the wound with soft cloths in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and make sure that the blood does not come out; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to the two methods of work: one method is that you cut tightly in front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have many different cuts, some sharp and others wide, and they are pointed and made of iron, and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
