Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the tooth is very hard and out of place, it is necessary that you drill around it, as well as administering cuts with trephines, but not so far that it goes through the bone; and above the point there should be a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each one corresponds to its own part of the bone, so that you have trephines for all parts of the bone.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	To pierce through the broken bone, you must place the iron over the bone and turn it to your left until you feel that the bone is pierced; then remove the iron to another part a little later, and so do all around, then cover the incisions the space of the bone between the periosteum, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take the bone in your hand, or in any of the instruments you have such as forceps, pliers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is advisable to remove any remaining small bones or scales from it with any instrument similar to a scalpel; but it must be more flexible and subtler than the other scalpel; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is as the Gauls say, which is more safe; and it is very good, and that is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you must remove a part of the bone where the fracture is open and wide, so that when you have uncovered that part, you can place the lens-shaped piece of this incision, which is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the broken piece is in two parts, so that the cutter is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer on top, so that you lightly copper the bone all around, and take care of the thread that is outside; if it is against the bone, then lightly cut the bone, because one cuts well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only broken from above, and there are small pieces, then you should smooth out that roughness, and remove scales with a sharp tool that you should have in various quantities to manage each limb as conveniently as possible, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have large razors, and then more sharp ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair and fine fracture trimmers, you should manage according to its convenience; and this is a thing that is not repeated to him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is exposed, it is necessary to apply a cloth of linen according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, so as not to irritate the wound, then administer by the side of the other liquid, and do not restrain it until it has only stained the wound; and leave it in this way for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour, incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make a powder and place it on the wound, and administer liquid medicines without irritation; and keep the wound clean, so that you do not leave any ointment, or any blood, for when blood gathers under the skin, it causes great pain and injury; because when something sharp is placed on the wound, it does not cure.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no accidents come to the patient, as we have said, it is uncertain with doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no other remedy comes to it except the one we have put on, which has virtue, then you must apply a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and an ounce of cloth, and put it on the wound; then treat the wound in ways that are suitable, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Note that the two parts of the nose above are never broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and the upper one is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary to break your small finger or nail of the finger, and place the broken part inside your index finger, and in the palm by default, until the finger regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and make sure the pain does not feel through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the broken part is in the upper part of the finger, and cannot reach the finger joint, it is necessary to place it on the tip of a needle or a slightly thick one.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the broken part is from both parts, make another one and hurry to restore the first joint, if you can; otherwise, after the seventh or eighth day, when the inflammation of the wound is calmed, then place it at the tip of the finger with pieces of linen cloth, if the broken part is in one piece.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you bend one way or the other, where the fracture is, and the bandages are so large that they fill the pores of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said no one should moisten the bandages in the morning, and each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is right, but it is necessary that they be moistened with a mixture of egg and powdered bread; then leave the bandage until the bone is hard, and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never use feathers instead of bandages, and if there is soft cloth around, hold the fractured part, and blow the pain away; now do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you work, put clay or cotton soaked in red wine or a drop of ichthyol into the nostril.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not come to the nose, then apply a poultice made of mustard flour and powdered frankincense mixed with egg yolk; then place light strips over it and do not tie the nose too tightly; and if the broken piece of the nose is small and in many pieces, then remove them with suitable instruments, then cut off the wound, and the cure of things embedded in charcoal and soldered, as suitable emplastres and ointments; and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents, and put in plasters until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured, and there is no wound elsewhere, and the fracture is not complete, but only slightly broken in two, because of the teeth inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right part, you should push your right little finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left jaw, push your right little finger with your right hand, and push the fracture inside lightly, and bring it to the other hand by default, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is in two parts, then it is necessary to administer traction of two parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth have occurred, or the breaking, then strain them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then place on the broken jaw, and place on the cloth a double layer; and place on the cloth a large well-made sheet, or a piece of leather even and wide according to the jaw, and tie it to the mouth so you can, and command the patient not to move, and give light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, then remove it to the other jaw, and then put back what is changing; and apply plaster on top, of flour from the mill with abundant honey or ground mustard, after having removed the cast; and place on the plaster another light layer, and if the plaster does not stick, let it remain until it becomes healed; often it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come to the head, then follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, cover no part of the bone with the flesh; instead, carefully remove the flesh from unsuitable tools.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none left, then clean the wound, if it is wide, and apply suitable bandages to stop bleeding until they are healed.
de la forcele	of the shoulder
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The shoulder bone breaks several times in front and behind the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: either it is broken and crushed into two pieces, and there are parts, and it is the least heavy to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the treatment when the fracture is with a wound, you should have two assistants, one to feel the shoulder bone broken; and the other to extend the neck to the part; then set the fracture to your hands, so that it is as it should be, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have the means to extend it further, place a rounded sphere of cloth or linen, as needed, against the shoulder at an angle; and stretch and relieve the pressure, and hold the sphere in your hand, so that you can align the break, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the shoulder blade back, because it comes out in front, then you must push the misaligned bones back over their surface, and place against the shoulder a hollow bone, and bend the minister's elbow down, until the bone of the shoulder blade is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then bring the fracture to your two ends, and if you have true teeth that are broken, it is necessary that you cut above; and carefully file the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined for any reason, use one of the instruments you have; but put the forceps of this instrument outside the wound to guard against the swelling.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not too sharp, and should also be as wide as needed, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the work; and have two prongs, one wide and the other narrow, as the edge of the wound that you made when you cut the bones; and when you are sure of an abscess, clean the wound, and if the wound is small, or you doubt an abscess, use dressings and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, if it is swollen, take a cloth dipped in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The splinting of the bone, when it is painful and swollen, is that you put on top of the bone the plaster of the mill flour and some egg, and put on top. Then take a very large bandage of one palm wide and long, then put the cloth double over the light dressing and the plaster; then take a thin strip of three inches wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the head of the bandage is hanging down; and put the strip on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and off the fracture, and off the fracture, and wrap each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture evenly, and you see clearly that the strip does not move over the broken bone, reward it every day, and when the bones are healed, hold it; and make the fracture lie on its back, and put what little oil is left from the fracture on top of the shoulder, to align the shoulder by the positioning of the arm, and not move the arm if no bad accidents happen within 20 days; then restart the plaster, if you see that it has a use, and tighten and leave it until it is healed; and it is healed in 28 days, and less to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder is broken or does not break in the middle, and it is only touched; then according to the figure of the fracture, and it is reset according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on the bone powder from the mill with abundant wheat flour, and light dressings, and put on a double cloth; then put on a wide and thin plate, a little larger than the shoulder, and if the plate is not in any part of the shoulder, then use a strip of linen so that the plate lies evenly; and then strongly bind it to all with a large bandage, so that the plate does not move from its place, and watch each day for the wound; and every time it breaks, if it is broken, and reset it if it is off its place, and dress the wound on its side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25. And when these numbers are completed, then release it, and be careful, for this is not bone that is put back firmly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is broken before the joint, and not completely separated from the bone, then cut through it, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the finger's joint to relieve an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the little finger
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The little finger is never broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the base.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines towards the outside, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of movement, and all, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the joint in the broken bone, and the patient feels well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the hairs are gently pulled up over their backs, and the cushion is placed between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades, and assemble the ribs of the two ribcages in your hands, and subtly put them back into all the positions you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place bandages and poultices on top of the thin salt sling, or some other light one, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so it does not move; then gently round the limb back to its position, and gradually tighten it, and every hour turn the limb, and if it moves, tighten it; and if it needs to be loosened, for corrosion or itching that comes to the skin, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and loosen it, and reapply the bandage, and treat whatever has come from the methods of healing; then reapply the bandage, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	that the rib fracturer comes only from large blows to the back and at the neck, and does not break easily because they are brittle; and the pain is felt well at the inspection of this.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are that you put the fracture back in place as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and the bandage of a splint if you know how to do it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is declining inwards, it causes great pain and sharpness, as if of piercing, because the ribs do not allow the needle; and it must be pricked, and everything and vomited a great deal of blood, and this is a very bad sickness, and the ancients have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the stomach, in order to push the fragment outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We should not make this mistake, unless an abscess is present.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it is present, then lance it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that no one should apply suction cups to the limb, for they draw out formations well, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt as to whether the cup will attract excess from the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that no one should cover the limb with a soft linen cloth in oil, and then place bandages between the ribs to even out the fluid inside, then treat the cure of pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pain is great that the patient cannot bear it due to the bone not being covered, and there is doubt, then you must cut across the broken rib on the side, and place a tool to hold back the tongue; and then you must break the bone, and gently pull it out, and then suture the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat them with ointments, until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes in the armpit, then place wet cloths moistened with rose oil on the affected area; and treat it as you would for an abscess, and let it lie near the chest where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No one ever breaks the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that they are damaged; and so with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens to anyone, and you want to know whether they will be healed or not, if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	It is often deadly in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when you hold them still and do not, then it is known that the joint of the bone is saved, and the pains are cured, if you put care on them.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you see whether it is healthy or not, if the feet are soft, and if the accidents that are in their hands, and above the back suddenly ventosity and egestion without will; and when they are laid on their belly, if suddenly egestion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is laid on its back and it wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is a deadly condition: do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to them, it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you reward him if he has an abscess that needs to be opened, and put rose oil or goose grease on the spine until it is relieved; then put one of the healing plasters that comforts and dries, and tie it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is decayed, it is necessary to cover it with a kerchief; then remove the bone, then gather the two edges of the wound, if they are large, into a seam, then treat the wound with char, until it is healed; and if the patient's bone is broken, which is called "the broken bone", if you have a handkerchief in your right hand, put it evenly on the other hand to your power, then put the plaster and the bandage on top, if you have the skill; then tighten it, and if there is decayed bone, do it again, and remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the rib of the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It is rare that the ribs of the back are broken, and if they are, it does not usually cause much discomfort to the head; and making it long, and declining to the waist, and coming to the pain in the limb, and swelling, and inflammation as it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as far as you are over the broken part; and cut away those parts that are broken and their shape; and if the break is only at the top, then set it straight until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it inclines towards the inside, then lay the limb across the patient's belly, until the restoration of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, apply the plaster, then place a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the fractured part still so it does not move; and keep the limb away from the sides, until the splint is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come, do not touch them until they are calmed down, and place on it what we have already mentioned; then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is located between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two methods: one is that you take a piece of bone from a single unbroken bone, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two broken pieces together and lift them up, and saw the painful part above the seat; then pour some brine on the broken piece of bone, as far as it will go, and add a hook of bone, then put something heavy on top; then put the broken pieces together in the hands together, until the broken person returns as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one pricks the pain above its shoulder, and places the hand on its neck, then commands two ministers to have one tattoo what is above the broken bone at his hands, and the other tattoos elsewhere to all that is connected, and stretches each to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, then hold the connected parts outside the broken bone, and above the broken bone, and stretch each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the broken bone is near the top of the shoulder, then it is necessary to place the connected parts outside the shoulder blade, and the other towards the back, outside the broken bone; and similarly if the broken bone is towards the back, then it is necessary to place the lighter parts gently, without labor, until the broken bone is even with the shoulder and the back, then set the fracture as it should be, and stretch it, if there are no signs of inflammation.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess appears and comes, if it is not held for seven days, and put in a poultice of milk and rose oil, until the abscess is relieved; then hold, and the manner of holding is that you place the plaster on the broken part, then assemble the arm above the support, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, and hold above the support, and above the arm, so that the arm is in its place, without anything defending it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and put on the break a wider and stronger splint than the others, and have between each splint two inches of space, and each splint is so large that it passes the broken part three fingers from each side; then hold above the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, stronger and less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the splint, and the binding, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess has healed, let it lie still for seven days, as we have said; then look at the joint every three hours, that it does not swell or become inflamed, or that the dislocations do not come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the splint, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents happen, then after three hours or more, let the patient lie on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put the aid in a cloth evenly, and look at the figure of the broken member every hour of the day or night, that it does not move, or that the joints are not softened; if the splint by the power of medicine, and give him the food we have previously put, in such a way that the food is at the first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	It is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset within 40 days of all; and then it is necessary to release and administer a bath and medicines of ointments for the limb to heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if its structure is ugly and deformed, it may take 1 or 2 months to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus" (the upper one is smaller and supports the elbow; the other is larger and is on the inside, towards the small bone). Sometimes only the large humerus breaks, or sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when large bones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it is best to extend them slightly and align them evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then it is best to stretch them more forcefully; and extend them upwards on the cushion, and the little fingers higher than the other fingers, and the small fingers lower than the other fingers, and the knuckles cross each other above themselves, and the cushion in front of him higher than the knuckles, so that the knuckles suffer no labor; then stretch the assistants' arms to the part outside his hand, or to the elbow, and other assistants to the top.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the mirrors evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is no suitable piece to hold the bone, you cannot restore it to its place, so do as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the broken piece there is a wound, I have spoken to the surgeon about it; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of restoration there is an abscess, then glue the cloth made of rose oil and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft; and tie the cloth gently until the abscess is soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the crust, and put on the poultice of the flour from the mill with abundant urine, then place the bandages, and make sure that the broken bone is held together more outside, and slightly wider than the others; and there should be six bandages or arms in more positions: whether the broken bone is in one of the bones, or in two; and held higher above the break than other parts, and always less away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are on the break be soft and moist, and not too hard or sharp; and let the thread, of which it is bound, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the limb and its joint after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accident occurs to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you raise the limb in hot water, until those itching are soothed; and leave the limb to rest without being tightly bound.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then continue the stretching, and if the joint is broken and the bones are displaced, and similar things, then advise.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the tendons cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, it is necessary that you soften it a little, and leave it like this for some time, until the tendons heal, and then stretch.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If none of these things we have said come to harm, it will not be until after twenty years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or if it is inside, then he can place his hands on his neck, and make his neck even, and guard against movement and dislocation, and sleep on his back; and after thirty years or thirty-five, or perhaps twenty years, depending on the constitutions and natures of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	However, at the back of the hand and with us, few breaks occur, and only rarely does it happen.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or dislocated, it should be straightened and set correctly in front of him equally; then place his hand on the extended palm, and stretch the broken bones, and put them even with the other fingers, until they are well jointed; and put on the plaster and compresses, if there is no swelling, then put a splint according to the size of the hand; and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the broken bone is in the middle of the foot plantar, make a bandage sphere and instruct the patient to wrap it around their broken foot; then stretch it into a long cloth, and let it be as wide as the palm of the hand, and stretch it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the broken bone is in the back, it is necessary to place a splint above and another below in the foot, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and stabilize the joint between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the broken bone is in one of the other fingers, if it is the thumb, straighten it as needed; and stretch it with the palm, and if you see that you need to place a small straight splint to lift the broken bone and not move; and if the broken bone is in the other fingers, such as the index or the others, straighten it and stabilize the joint with the finger next to it; or tie them all together while holding them, which is better, or place a splint above, depending on whether it is the thumb; and take care of the restoration and positioning of abscesses, and support what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken ribs
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the ribcage are often broken, and one can see it when they turn in front and behind; and the restoration is such that one lies on the side of the breaker, and the other outside.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the pain is set on their face, then each minister stretches their limb equally to their part; and it is when the break is brought to the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the ribcage, then one lies on the side of the breaker, and the other limbs outside.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And thus if it is near the groin, and then the joints above the groin are stretched out, and the extension is below; then place the bone evenly in both hands, as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, and no abscess comes.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess, let it settle down then return to your work and your treatment; the bandage is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the fractured part doubled in two or three times, and let the excess remain, then bend the leg so that the toes come to the root of the knee, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg below the groin, and bring the top of the thread above; then bend over the leg and the thigh, the bandage, then place the bandage on the fractured part, and put a strip of cloth on the bone of the leg; then fill the wool between the leg and the thigh to make the pressure even, then begin to tie three or four times above the fracture; and as you go higher than the fracture, and less the pressure; then feel the two threads that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and the three strips that are above, then return to the top of the thread, until you come below the knee; and the pressure, so that it does not move from its place, then let it remain like this, so that there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it is broken, and it dislocates, and address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that can be felt, then it should be set, if possible; and if not, then it must be broken, and traction applied; and the cure as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the rib broken in such a way that these ribs are placed, as in the dislocation and arm; however, in the restoration thus made does not hurt the hairs.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And the ribs are restored at different times, a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin path
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	There is little breakage in the groin path, but it often causes pain.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	If it breaks, it is only a small cut, or a puncture, and it causes pain to all wounds, and without pain, and it feels bad.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put what is broken back together as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and if you have skill, put on a round bandage, and hold it in place as it should be, then treat all the dispositions that we have said for other fractures, such as abscess and similar things; and for each accident, put what is necessary until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" on the right, and the other is called "foscile"; and all the fractures come out as they do in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the work is all there. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg returns to its normal state from all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then it returns in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then great pain is felt, and it can be seen well; and it returns outside.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, apply counter-extension, and make it even, and tie the fractured parts equally; however, if there is a break and it is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the extension should be less and lighter; and the alignment according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that bind the leg on one side and the other, and be long enough to cover the leg from the knee to the ankle; then wrap them above and below, and tie in the middle as well, and at this point the leg will not bend to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one administers the long cloth of the leg, and it is made of, and properly place the leg to prevent movement, and correctly done they put it in the fracture where it has a wound; and move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or other accident; if the cure as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of bone fractures of the skull
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but in the skull, bone fractures never occur and it is very rare, and there are only a few cases of dislocation.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the skull bones, and you see these bones overlying each other, then place them back on the ground as if they were walking, then put your bone over where the bones are raised, then press it until it returns to its original position; then apply the plaster and wash it with water, and put a small cloth soaked in the patient's plain on the belly of the skull, then strap the skull evenly, then wrap bandages around it and other things that you have experience with.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the joint is dislocated, you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or displaced.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the broken bones, if you set them as we have said for both hands; then place a splint along the length of the broken bone, and make it slightly wider, then place the bandage as I have described, and tighten it evenly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, place a splint for each one according to its quantity, wrapped in a piece of linen, and tie the bandage from above the splints so that it covers the wound well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as soon as we have mentioned; and treat each accident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of the woman are broken, if the wound is enlarged, then incline it to the back part, and hold it by the back; then fill the wound with cotton, and put in as much as possible; then raise the woman, and lift the back slowly and slowly, and then the cotton will come out of the natural opening, and the bone with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, return it, and thus do this for seven days or around: if it is restored, and if you see, take a bladder of lamb’s wool, and tie a catheter to a needle, and blow all the bladder into the natural opening; then blow into the catheter formally, until the bladder is inflated inside: nature will restore the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it in this way for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the little finger of the hand is broken, or of the woman, if it is reset as we have said in the bone of the shoulder; and these broken fragments are not hidden from him who puts his study and practice to it, and attends my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the broken bone means in many positions the right way of restoration: understand therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the thigh, when it is broken, take a goose neck and beat the thigh; then wrap it in cloths, and leave it for three days or around, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has fracture with wound, especially if it is large, such as the bones of the ribs or shoulder or similar, that they be cleaned immediately, so that the cleanings that we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, and if there is no other thing, then begin to restore the fractured bone in the same hour, or the next day, if there are no complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if complications arise, then leave the restoration until the next day, until the complications are soothed, and do not touch it on that day or the following, for you would bring about bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken jaw appears to be displaced, then you must gently place it back in position with your hands, extending it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not available to place in your hands, then use the iron instrument that is seven or eight spans long, according to the size of the wound; and the width should be according to the quantity of the wound; and it is necessary for the mire to have three or four, according to what it has in each case of fracture; and it should be round and a little thick, so that it does not pierce through the member at your work, and it should be sharp in front, and wide in the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the patient must have the broken bone placed above the head of the visible bone; and the bone is pushed once, as much as it returns, and they are evenly spaced one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone until the instruments have hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, then use an appropriate tool, such as a saw or chisel, to your power; then file off what remains in the bone of sharpness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is returned, and the pain is great afterwards, do not let it remain in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do this until it is in its natural place, then wipe the bone with black stiptic wine, and properly if it has been broken; and do not put anything on the wound except oil, that it does not cause pus and corruption to come forth; then administer these things as soon as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not strained with the breakage; many times this has been done by fools, and they have caused pus or death or corrosion to come forth.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that no harm has come to it, as we have said, and if you relieve pain at the limb, then it does not need to be elevated; but wrap around it, in place of elevation, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is beginning to open again, remove what you have put on top of everything, and apply healing ointment, such as triple antibiotic ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you move the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be arranged in such a way that the bow can move freely.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue to overstep, and it cannot be fixed but remains bent, with small pieces of bone, for which it is necessary that you take the wound with a tent, and remove all these unwanted pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the limb, or another kind of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it according to what it says in its previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open in the limb, like the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not pull it out, for many times it kills, but let it stay as long as it can; perhaps it will fall off after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	brutal blows that come from the forging
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see them after the health of the forger, even when it is near the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps they cannot do their natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, if we find that it is fresh, then administer stypic medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollis, acaice, and similar things, either one or all together, and mix them with stypic wine or abundant oil or vinegar; and place it on the nail in an enema, and hold it well, and do not let it slip into the hands later; then remove it, and start another until the swelling is gone; or you hold a piece of raw meat well made; for the property of the raw meat is that it removes all the swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, if the cope above, and making the superfluity apparent; or you cut it with a knife until it is removed, and care for it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb after a dislocation
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and the limb remains weak and subtle afterward, this can be due to many causes: one is because it was too tightly bound, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and could not bring the members together to the limb; or because of too much swelling; or because of too great movements, not in its time; or because it has little blood in its body, then it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.
