And the cure is that you make the pain less, and make the body tense, until the swelling is not multiplied in it; and administer baths, and give joy and ease; then put poultices on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great swelling, and the swelling often of hot water, until the swelling goes to the limb; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the limb is deformed, yet it does not affect its natural appearance: therefore do not believe those who say that one must break the limb entirely, and many have done this in our land; and these practices are blamed, and great harm comes from them, and perhaps death; however, if the fractures and deformities are fresh, it is necessary to apply hot, or softening herbs boiled, such as willow bark, roots, and meadowsweet, and similar things; and the mollifying plaster, such as made with good hydromel, and take the willow bark powder, and mix it with goose grease or sesame oil, and apply the plaster; or take figs, and grind them with linseed, and similar medicines that alleviate the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation caused by continuously and long rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is awake and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be removed with the iron, if it fits under the bone, make a shallow incision; and put on a bandage and rest in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to any joint, it must now be returned to its proper place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, the joint may swell, and if it is reset, it may return to its incorrect place; for it does not matter that it moves as it is swollen: many times, spasms and other pains are brought on; therefore, when this happens, first cleanse the wound, then leave it until the abscess has been soothed; then raise the limb with hot and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as it comes back to its proper place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations of the shoulder joint down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are two ways in which the mandibles can be dislocated: either they are slightly displaced from their place and somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and preventing the tongue from holding saliva, nor can it close its mouth, and enveloping the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns on its own in various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is completely and fully dislocated, then you must reset it urgently, and do not delay; and in this manner, the healer should apply pressure on the painful part of the jaw, and insert a small piece of cloth into the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand should be outside, to hold evenly; and command the patient to soften his jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And when the bone is uneven, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially when both mandibles are together, using hot and oil, until it moves slightly; do not force the resetting as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the jaw pain is relieved by softening, put a cloth made of melted wax and rosin on the molded dough; then tie it lightly with moistened linen strips; and let the patient sleep on his back, with his head between two pillows, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor strain himself to turn, but take light food, until the pain is gone, and the jaw is healed; then change what he wants lightly, and do not force him to open his mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be reset to their proper position within an hour, and they are not converted back to their usual alignment, then fevers and sweats become customary, and perhaps diarrhea, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then cut it out as it is fatal; and many times those who have had it die within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the forcelle (a type of medical instrument)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forcelle cannot be extracted from the side without cutting through the continuation of the skin and the flesh, and it is never removed unless necessary, and well one can feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the hairs are gently pulled back over their backs, and they extend their arms; then press the joint firmly into your palm, and it will return; then place the plaster and bandage, and hold it tight; and the one who is on the side cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates once, then reset the joint as we have said; then place the plaster and bandage, and hold it tight, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and thus the same is returned to the shoulder, when it is free from its joint.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways that the shoulder can be dislocated: one is that it dislocates at the part of the armpit outwards; and the second is at the part of the elbow; and by chance it dislocates at the part above, and this happens little; and it does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the arm; and often it dislocates outwards towards the armpit, especially to those who have little strength, because for these it is done forcefully; and for those who have enough strength, it dislocates easily, and returns easily.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some men, percussion or fracture, and inflames the shoulder with an abscess, and thinks it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must examine him until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocation is when it is below the acromion, and it distinguishes between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them manifest differences; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a depression, and below the acromion the top of the shoulder, as if it were an ace; and the bad hand cannot move its finger, nor any movement; and also, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you will see it manifestly at the back; and this way of dislocation is only to be reset when it is new, or when the pain is severe.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister lifts the hand of the injured person up, then puts his fingers below the joint, and pulls the joint upwards to the shoulder; and the minister lifts the hand, and extends it up, so he puts it away; then it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said before, then it is necessary that the injured hand be soaked in hot water; and the minister should apply a softening and soothing lotion, such as a decoction of sage and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and apply it; then place the injured hand on its back, and put a cloth of even thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, under the joint, then put the foot of the injured hand on the cloth, and lift the shoulder gently, and pull the hand; and other ministers wet the head of the injured hand, so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder is now completely set, and if you see that it is reset correctly: and you must make sure that there is someone who is taller than the injured person; and they should stand to the side of the chest, and pull the shoulder of the injured hand away from the joint, and lift the joint upwards, so that the injured hand hangs in the air; and other ministers take the hand of the injured person down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the pain is too light, with it there can be nothing heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also done in another way: and it is thus that one puts a long stick on the ground, where the patient can be held as with a spear, and not too heavy or too rough; then it is placed away from the pain, but with a soft cloth over it, and the pain should be at the long end of the stick; then extend your hand down from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take a stick of two arms wide and four fingers high, which has the head round at one end, like this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie a soft cloth over the shoulder where the dislocation occurred, which was not causing the pain, then remove it from the dislocated area; extend your arm over the long one, and tie the helper over the dislocated arm, and the hand at the head of the hand, then place your arm over the broad side of a broad arrow, and stretch your hand downwards, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joint is now healed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when she is ready, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary that you place a soft cloth over the shoulder, then apply the plaster mixed with powder from the mill, with incense and a little honey, over the entire shoulder and around, then remove the cloth from the shoulder evenly, and return the limb to the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he change little, as long as the limbs are comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then change after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiff and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is very weak due to moisture that has come, or for other reasons, it is necessary that you administer cauteries at three places, as it is placed in front or in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm above, then cut the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and cut that the joint has never been fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs above the knee and behind the elbow, or below, is caused by impact and stretching of the hands, and it requires another lubricant; and it should be treated until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb swells and moves slowly, then frequently apply compresses to the affected area until the swelling is reduced and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	The joint of the shoulder is repeatedly dislocated and returns to its place; and it is dislocated from all parts, both in front and behind, and the dislocation does not return, for one can see and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with its joint, see it clearly open.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is cut, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it as soon as the joint swells up, for if the joint swells up and comes back, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset completely at once, especially when it is in the back; it is better than other dislocations, but causes greater pain, and perhaps many die.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the resetting is, when it can be reset, that you extend your hand to both of their hands; and their arms are spread out, and their hands like a mirror around the shoulder, back and forth, and push the joint to its knuckles together, or at the root of their palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand over his hand, and holds onto the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to the joint, then apply strong extension; and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and tie it with two ministers, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from each part, then when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when you see the joint at the joint of his hand, if he holds any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint together, as long as it returns; and when it is in place, put some dry plaster with some honey on top, and press it together, and put the arm on the shoulder of the bad side, and leave it for some time, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then restart the bandage and the ligament, and leave it thus for some time, until it is firmly put back in place; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub him well, and press until it is relieved; or place a thick lamb fat on the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and put in a bath; and when he urinates, rub the joint immediately, then place the fat back on, and put him in the bath again; do this twice or three times until he is healthy; and if you see that it does not return to its position, then place moist warm water with butter on it, and strain it; then it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	the joint of the hand dislocates, and the return is lighter than other joints; therefore, it must be reset quickly in the same place as it is dislocated, as long as the limb is swollen or there is an abscess forming.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is done by placing the misaligned hand on a table, extending the fingers of the hand, and aligning the palm so that it is over the appearance of the joint; then press it until it returns to its place; therefore, it is necessary to check if it is properly aligned; then place the misaligned hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's hand on a table, and the practitioner places their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good; if not, apply warm compresses to abscesses, and leave it thus to begin again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if it cannot be borne, and you cannot put it back in place after some time, the joint will remain twisted; and do not force anything into the wound until the hand is clean, and nothing can be forced in at all: then cut the tendon or artery; if there is no other means but to cauterize over the bone, and perhaps nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is dislocated, put the plaster that we have mentioned on it, then strain and leave it for five days, then release and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no swelling, pour hot vinegar on it and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of both hands
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Both hands are never dislocated at any part, not at the back of the palm or the belly; therefore, both hands are held, and reset the dislocation to your fists until it returns, then support the head of the hand, and push it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, and then put it back that day; and tie it as we have said, and loosen it on the next day, and move it, and rejoin it; and do this often, until it is straightened, and do the same if it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in other parts.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	back dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or neck is dislocated, and there are many dislocations, there is no cure, for the patient dies from the pain.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the excretions suddenly jump without volition, cannot be held, and often all the limbs become soft, or the two arms or the right arm or left, and often the spine moves in four directions; this movement is called "gibbering": the cure is to reward the gibberer if it comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing for the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And the one that comes from falling or from impacts or similar things, they said in ancient ways of cures with great words, where there is not much benefit; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the case of a fracture that comes from the front, there is no engineering or healing; and also the one that comes directly to the second rib, and one cannot cure it other than the proper one that comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the hairs should be stretched out over his face in one even layer, and have some straw away from him, so he does not bleed; then make a bandage at the head in earth form, and the other at the feet, and tie one ligature outside the fracture, and the other at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and the assistant should fasten the ligatures, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two bandages; and they should be well tied, the bandage as we have said, and the hands put his palms on the spine correctly, until he recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a three-armed mallet and strike it from the side, and the hairs should be on the side, and bring the middle of the mallet above the spine; then place the patient's feet on the other end of the mallet, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see, do the same with the turnbuckle that turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should place two ropes at the head of the shoulder of one arm and two more by the feet, and between each rope, outside and inside, a palm of long hair; and in each rope, one nail, or the turnbuckle is correct, and the ropes are firmly on the ground so that they do not move; and between each two ropes, one turning rope, along with the turnbuckles, and two small ropes of a palm of long hair to turn the turnbuckle; and then tie the ligament that is among the tendons to the turnbuckle towards the head, and the other ligament towards the feet to the other turnbuckle, and each minister turns his turnbuckle along the whole ligament, and the masters put the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, apply a drying ointment with an abundance of honey, and then insert a probe, and then place the back of a three-finger-width thick board on the affected area and the part of the spine, as we have said, and use subtle pressure, until it is healed; and if nothing comes to the end of health, then administer medicines that are softening and soothing, with the treatment we have mentioned before; and never give one piece of plaster, and never does an appearance come in the lower spine of the back, and be careful not to assume it is dislocation; and this is the bone that opens, for if there is presumption, it may cause death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Unlike the joints of the hip and shoulder, which only occur as dislocations and not as other joint issues; and the hip joint is misaligned in four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside than that, and slightly misaligned in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of this dislocation inside is that when the crooked leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and more open than the healthy ones, and cannot bend its knee to the fire; and the legs that are below are inflamed with abscesses, because the cause of the belly comes from there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes after this is that this accident is opposite to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has come before are that he will have his leg properly set; however, if the knee is bent with pain, and if one wants to make it move, it cannot be done, and he retains his urine, and swells up, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has come after are that he cannot spread his knee, nor bend it, and the other leg is more twisted than the other, and the swelling is softened, and the shoulder is dislocated from the side of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The symptoms of this type of dislocation are such that if it is ancient, and it remains according to its position, there is no cure; and there should be no presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of four types of dislocation, you must turn the joint back, and extend and flex it, and move it to the right and left; perhaps if it returns, and there is no other cure needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must apply two strong ministers, and extend the leg strongly to both sides, or to one that is tied above the knee; and some other ministers place their hand below the chin in a certain manner so that they bite their hands off from their sockets, then hold them with a rope attached to the side; and some grip the head of the limb; and extend up and down all at once, until the pain is lifted from the ground once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must take care of its similar case. When the dislocation is in the pardedens, you should support the misaligned limb on its sound side, then place the ligament at the base of the elbow, and the limb that is outside the angle, then extend the ligament above the angle and towards the forearm; then take other ministers to grasp the large arm of the misaligned elbow, and extend it in a proper form: if it returns to its place, this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you do not hold it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary to bind the two hairs together with a strong string above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the badly placed leg be stretched out two fingers more than the other; then hang it suspended by the head of a stick, and let the arms be stretched out two arms' length from the ground; then command the minister to grasp the back of the neck, and let another minister hold the badly placed leg, who should grasp it firmly, for the joint is now approaching.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is gone, then massage the hairs, as we have said in the one with gout, and pull the ligament above the badly placed leg properly, and on the foot also; then put two ties, one at the head and one at the foot, then tie the rope between the thighs of the badly placed leg in the correct form; and wrap moist cloths around it, so that it does not swell up, then each minister should stretch out towards it, and the master place the dislocation equally in his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a flat surface, and press it in this way as we have described in the booklet, and grind the hairs against the clean surface.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the injured leg vigorously, as I have described; and place your hand on the painful part of the limb, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not necessary to stretch the injured limb downwards or lift it up, but it should be as it was when dislocated from the back, as we have described for the supine position on the two hips; and it should be supported on its face, and the limb extended as we have described before, and one should press on the joint at the table; and it will be perfect when the injured limb extends its legs, and they are even; then bend the knees, and apply the plaster, and the strap of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then release it, and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are even, remove the strap, as before, and leave it for three days; then release it, and let the limb move, until the member is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the hip, and if he cannot bend it at the hip, then it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back against his face, and put his foot on yours; then take his shoulder to your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the shoulder correctly; and another minister extends his foot, until the shoulder returns to its place, and the sign is that he can bend his leg at the hip lightly; and put the plaster on it, and bear the leg against the hip, and tie them together strongly for three or four hours, then release; and do not work on the patient any further until the member is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	If the limbs are not properly aligned, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the back, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocated ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are never sprained and never fully dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the bone is swollen, and feels tender to the touch in the place where it is dislocated: the pain is slight, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is sprained only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully dislocated, you should first straighten the pain correctly, and hold it with your hands, above the ankle; then pull the bone towards you twice, then extend it upwards, and hit it hard on the top; and do this twice, as we have said, pulling and pushing the bone; if it returns, it is good; if not, start the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, put the pain on its back on the ground, and firmly press between its knees, and wrap cloths around it so that it does not bend the pain; then hold the hands of the ministers to the knee, and other ministers extend the bone to their hands or to the tie, so that they hold the collar of the bone; then extend all the ministers equally, and the cloths should be placed between the knees of the pain to hold the pain while it is extended; then put the hands equal to the dislocation at its hands, and other ministers hold the leg straight outside, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when she does not go through, apply the plaster and soak it above, and let the strain form, and tie the foot to the leg, and hold the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the joints are not too tight; then leave her for two or three days, and if the joints dislocate, apply the plaster again; then release it on the third or fourth day, and let it walk for four days; and if it goes before this term, it is not sure that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, it is necessary to calm them as we have said before, until they are healed.
des dois	For the fire cautery, instruct
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	when the two are dislocated, if they must be stretched out, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no way on the inside or outside of the joint, it is necessary that you make the patient sit with the affected limb straight out or on a table, and put your hand on what opens up from these joints, then press firmly, until it returns; and when it is even, and there is nothing open, put the sole of the foot on a table at II o'clock, then stretch it firmly, and leave it for three hours, then release; and let him rest, until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and of dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often many die: if you are not very presumptuous in the cure, and you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and patient and slow; at the beginning of things, use gentle things to calm the abscess, and leave the pain in God’s hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the member now, as soon as the abscess comes; and when the member is in place, then administer gentle things to calm the abscess, and cure the wound, as it should be, with frequent dressings; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are shattered, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, for it is better for you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your weapon and your body.
Amen	For the fire cautery
